       <h2>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="About_this_Wiki">
         About this Wiki
        </span>
       </h2>
       <p>
        The E46 Wiki should be used as a tool to help all E46 owners.  The greatest feature of the Wiki is that anyone with an account on Bimmerfest has the ability to edit it.  See something incorrect or notice something missing?  Simply click on the edit link to the right of any section.   To discuss changes to the Wiki, post a message
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=156315" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        This Wiki was primarily authored by
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/member.php?u=112/" rel="nofollow">
         KrisL
        </a>
        -
        <a class="external free" href="http://www.linquist.net" rel="nofollow">
         http://www.linquist.net
        </a>
        .   If you like my posts or the information I provide, please use me as your referrer (Kris Linquist #170334) when joining the
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmwcca.org" rel="nofollow">
         BMW Car Club of America
        </a>
        ($48/yr).  The BMW CCA offers a great magazine with tech tips, high-performance driving schools, car control clinics, autocrosses, social events, and even $500+ off of your next new or CPO BMW after you've been a member for a year (independent of the dealer transaction!).   When you join the BMW CCA, you'll automatically become a member of your local chapter.  I am a car control driving instructor and autocross coordinator for the
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.ggcbmwcca.org" rel="nofollow">
         Golden Gate Chapter
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        Have a question not answered here? Check out the discussion forums at
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/forumdisplay.php?f=98" rel="nofollow">
         Bimmerfest
        </a>
        and
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.E46Fanatics.com/" rel="nofollow">
         E46Fanatics
        </a>
        or
        <a class="external text" href="http://bimmerforums.com" rel="nofollow">
         BimmerForums
        </a>
       </p>
       <h2>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="E46_Summary">
         E46 Summary
        </span>
       </h2>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="What_is_an_E46.3F">
         What is an E46?
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Each BMW body style is assigned a two digit number preceeded by "E". The "E" stands for "Entwicklung", the German word for development. The E46 is the body style for the following models (USA model listing except where noted):
       </p>
       <div style="float: left; width: 500px; padding:1em;">
        <ul>
         <li>
          316i - sedan - 1999 through 2005 model years (available in EU only)
         </li>
         <li>
          318i - sedan - 1999 through 2001 model years (available in EU only)
         </li>
         <li>
          320i - sedan - 2000 through 2004 model years (available in EU and Canada only)
         </li>
        </ul>
        <hr/>
        <ul>
         <li>
          323i - sedan - 1999 through 2000 model years
         </li>
         <li>
          323Ci - coupe - 2000 model year only
         </li>
         <li>
          323Cic - convertible - 2000 model year only
         </li>
         <li>
          323iT - wagon - 2000 model year only
         </li>
        </ul>
        <hr/>
        <ul>
         <li>
          328i - sedan - 1999 through 2000 model years
         </li>
         <li>
          328Ci - coupe - 2000 model year only
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div style="float: left; width: 500px; padding:1em;">
        <ul>
         <li>
          325i - sedan - 2001 through 2005 model years
         </li>
         <li>
          325Ci - coupe - 2001 through 2006 model years
         </li>
         <li>
          325Cic - convertible - 2001 through 2006 model years
         </li>
         <li>
          325iT - wagon - 2001 through 2005 model years
         </li>
         <li>
          325xi - sedan - all wheel drive - 2001 through 2005 model years
         </li>
         <li>
          325xiT - wagon - all wheel drive - 2001 through 2005 model years
         </li>
        </ul>
        <hr/>
        <ul>
         <li>
          330i - sedan - 2001 through 2005 model years
         </li>
         <li>
          330Ci - coupe - 2001 through 2006 model years
         </li>
         <li>
          330Cic - convertible - 2001 through 2006 model years
         </li>
         <li>
          330xi - sedan - all wheel drive - 2001 through 2005 model years
         </li>
        </ul>
        <hr/>
        <ul>
         <li>
          M3 - coupe - 2001 through 2006 model years
         </li>
         <li>
          M3 - convertible - 2001 through 2006 model years
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <br style="clear:both;"/>
       <p>
        The 2006 3 Series sedan and 2007 3 Series coupe are the new body style, the E90.
       </p>
       <p>
        <br/>
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Changes_throughout_the_E46_run">
         Changes throughout the E46 run
        </span>
       </h3>
       <hr/>
       <div style="float: left; width: 500px; padding:1em;">
        <dl>
         <dt>
          Changes from 1999 to 2000
         </dt>
        </dl>
        <ul>
         <li>
          E46 Coupe launched
         </li>
         <li>
          DSC replaces ASC (different traction control systems)
         </li>
         <li>
          Auto Recirculation becomes standard
         </li>
         <li>
          Light Yellow Metallic will replace Sea Green
         </li>
         <li>
          There will be a red interior offered
         </li>
         <li>
          The 323 will have 15" Alloy wheels standard (replacing hub caps for no-option package 323s)
         </li>
         <li>
          The Premium pkg will have wood trim and moonroof standard, with 16" wheels only (no more 15" offered)
         </li>
         <li>
          The 323 will get the Sport/Premium combo package offered
         </li>
         <li>
          Coupes get Topaz Blue as a color option
         </li>
         <li>
          Power seats are a stand-alone option on 323

        </ul>

         </li>

          Moonroof will be standard in the sport wagon.
         </li>
         <li>
          Emission regulations established by the California Air Resources Board (CARB) required BMW to sell vehicles with new emission standards in California, Massachusetts, New York and Vermont. In order to comply with these regulations, starting MY03 BMW sold Super Ultra Low Emission Vehicles (SULEV) in these four states.
          <ul>
           <li>
            BMW offered three SULEV models in the states mentioned above: 325i sedan, sport wagon and coupe (equipped with automatic transmission). There were no AWD SULEV models. For ordering purposes in the four states mentioned, these three SULEV vehicles had their own model designations.
           </li>
           <li>
            The difference between SULEV and non-SULEV vehicles extended beyond the emissions rating.  Arguably the most important was the warranty:  an extensive emissions warranty covers far more.  It lasts 15-years and 150,000-miles with no deductible.  Some of the differences are obvious (the engine looks different), others not so much: the fuel tank is metal instead of plastic (for evaporative emissions purposes).  Originally, only automatic transmission 325 models could be SULEV vehicles, but this changed with the E90 model transition where either transmission could be a SULEV.)
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
        </ul>
        <p>
         330 models:

It will only be available in conjunction with the sport package. SMG will not be available in conjunction with the Performance Package or all-wheel drive models.
          <ul>
           <li>
            E46 SMG models were remarkably rough-shifting and problematic.  They sold poorly as a result.  Very few were ordered and this option was later dropped.  While the SMG system used on the 325 was not the same system as used on the M3, both have poor reputations.  For full details see the various long-term tests of these drive train combinations in Car and Driver, Automobile, and other enthusiast magazines.)
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
        </ul>
        <dl>
         <dt>

         </li>
        </ul>

        </dt>
       </dl>

        </li>

        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        Sedan and wagon:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         The rain sensor and automatic headlight control standard for all Sedans and Sports Wagons. These features were previously only available with the Premium Package (ZPP).
        </li>
        <li>

        </li>
        <li>
         New Sport Package wheel for 325i Sedan and Sports Wagon. Styling 119 replaces Styling 96.
        </li>
        <li>
         New base wheel for the 330i/330xi Sedan and 325xi Sedan/Sports Wagon when equipped with the Sport Package. New wheel replaces Styling 73.
        </li>
        <li>
         Titanium exterior trim on the front grille and headlights will no longer be a differentiator for 330i and 330xi Sedans. (The headlights will be black and the front spoiler will be a combination of black and body color.)
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        Coupes and Convertibles:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Coupes and convertibles receive a major face lift with a new front grille (larger "BMW kidneys"), revised cleaner looking lower bumper design and front/rear light design including LED tail lights, repositioned side turn signal lights and clear front corners on sport package cars.
        </li>
        <li>
         The Xenon headlight package was upgraded to the Adaptive Xenon package for coupes/convertibles only.
         <ul>
          <li>
           Adaptive Xenons not only auto-level as the standard Xenons do, but they also rotate side-to-side depending on orientation of the steering wheel. The goal is to point the light in the direction the car is traveling. A complex algorithm uses car speed, wheel angle, etc. to determine where to point the lights. Of interesting note is the fact that when the car is not moving, the lights will not turn to the driver's side (this is to avoid potential blinding of oncoming traffic, e.g. at a stop light). The headlight switch must be in the "A" (automatic) position -- turning the headlight switch to the "On" position will auto-level the headlights and turn them on, but they will be fixed straight ahead and not turn left and right.
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        325i and 325i Sports Wagon:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Styling 119 (17 x 8) with performance tires replaces Styling 96 when the sport package (ZSP) is ordered. This aligns the 325i with the 325Ci. Now all rear-wheel drive 325 models have the same Sport Package Wheel.
        </li>
        <li>
         MY2004 330i/330xi Sedan Base wheel. 325xi and 325xi Sports Wagon Sport Package wheel.
        </li>
        <li>
         Styling 137 (17 x 7) with all-season tires replaces Styling 73, also known as the Radial spoke.
        </li>
       </ul>

        <dt>

        </dt>

         <ul>
          <li>
           The change was made about halfway through the 2005 model year and driven primarily by the inability of the alcantara wheel to hold up well over time.  Prior to May 2005, Performance Package 330s shipped with alcantara, after that they shipped with a perforated leather wheel.  Many originally-alcantara Performance Package 330s, however, will have had the alcantara wheel swapped out for leather under warranty due to excessive wear of the alcantara.
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
        <li>
         Lumbar seat support added to the premium package on the 325.
        </li>
       </ul>

       <p>
        <br/>
       </p>
       <h2>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Buying_an_E46">
         Buying an E46
        </span>
       </h2>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="How_durable_or_reliable_is_the_E46.3F_Is_it_expensive_to_own.3F">
         How durable or reliable is the E46? Is it expensive to own?
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Given that the average E46 is 7+ years old, this is a particularly common concern for prospective buyers.
       </p>
       <p>
        To begin with, "reliability" means different things to different people. To some, a car that starts and runs and doesn't break down
        <i>
         frequently
        </i>
        would be considered reliable. To others, a "reliable" car is one that runs forever with little or no maintenance. The E46 is of the former--the engines and most of the drivetrain components are first class, though unfortunately there are also peripheral components of questionable design and/or production quality which are likely to fail. If you want or expect a car that will get you where you need to go (provided it is properly maintained), an E46 will do that. If you want a car that you can abuse or neglect, or one that will be absolutely free of any sort of minor nuisance or defect, look elsewhere.  That being said, unlike some other BMW's models, the E46 does
        <b>
         not
        </b>
        have particularly problematic electronics; "gremlins" are unusual. Virtually all of the model's common problems are now well documented, and most are actually fairly easy to diagnose and repair.
       </p>
       <p>
        The following E46/BMW components can be considered highly dependable (Least likely to cause issues):
       </p>
       <div style="border-left: 0.2em solid #3CABB2; margin-left: 0.5em; padding-left: 0.5em;">
        <ul>
         <li>
          Engine
         </li>
         <li>
          Manual transmission and differentials
         </li>
         <li>
          Interior materials and furnishings (instrumentation, lighting, radio headunits, etc)
         </li>
         <li>
          Body panels/glass/paint/rust resistance
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <p>
        The following components are reasonably dependable but do occasionally suffer from minor or seemingly unusual issues (which are generally cheap and/or easy to resolve):
       </p>
       <div style="border-left: 0.2em solid #3CABB2; margin-left: 0.5em; padding-left: 0.5em;">
        <ul>
         <li>
          Suspension: certain bushings are wear/failure prone by design--this is more of a problem for people unaccustomed to high performance cars
         </li>
         <li>
          Automatic heating/air conditioning
         </li>
         <li>
          Audio speakers and most accessory electronics
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <p>
        The following components are relatively suspect:
       </p>
       <div style="border-left: 0.2em solid #3CABB2; margin-left: 0.5em; padding-left: 0.5em;">
        <ul>
         <li>
          Engine cooling system: water pump, thermostat, expansion tank
         </li>
         <li>
          Accessory pulleys and tensioners
         </li>
         <li>
          Automatic transmissions, particularly in early model years
         </li>
         <li>
          ZKW brand HID/xenon headlamps (most cars have AL/Bosch, particularly those built before 2003)
         </li>
         <li>
          Window lifters/regulators (the mechanical apparatus that physically lifts or lowers the glass side windows) and sunroof shade guides
         </li>
         <li>
          Rear subframe, primarily (but not absolutely limited to) the early model year cars (model years 1999-2000--i.e. ALL 323/328 sedan/coupes). Convertibles and Wagons of all years have least reports of failure. For all models, it is important to verify subframe and differential bushings are in good shape so there is minimal play in heavy drivetrain components which could further stress the subframe mounting area.
         </li>
        </ul>
        <p>
         (
         <i>
          See
          <a href="/wiki/index.php/BMW_E46#What_should_I_look_out_for.3F" title="BMW E46">
           What should I look out for?
          </a>
          and the sections on Cooling System, Maintenance, Engine, etc. for more information.
         </i>
         )
        </p>
       </div>
       <p>
        Cost of upkeep varies wildly. The E46 is not an exotic car per se, and does not generally require any special service techniques beyond any other typical import car, though dealerships and many third party shops will attempt to bill you as though it is. Without question, you will save a significant sum of money by performing your own simple repairs and routine maintenance; meanwhile, paying dealership/shop prices for window regulator repairs and blower resistor pack replacements will make it difficult to justify the cost of ownership.
       </p>
       <p>
        Bottom line, budget about $1000 per year for repairs and maintenance (including tires, brakes, oil, etc) if you perform the maintenance yourself. If you intend to have a third party perform all work, you might realistically expect to spend 2-3x this amount.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="What_should_I_look_out_for.3F">
         What should I look out for?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        The E46 doesn't have many significant problem areas and is generally a durable vehicle; however if the car was not maintained at by the PO, you can expect numerous problems just like any used and abused car. If you are going to buy a used E46, avoid cars without a good maintenance and repair history. Luckily, the E46 had free maintenance until 36,000 or 50,000 miles (depending on year), so most early maintenance was performed by BMW dealers. Any dealer should be able to provide the service history with just the last seven digits of the VIN.
       </p>
       <p>
        Below are some typically and well known issues:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         <b>
          Window regulators
         </b>
         - The windows will then either make clicking noises as they go up/down (sign of a failing regulator) or not operate at all possibly leaving your window partially or fully open. This is an extremely common failure and a clear weakspot on the E46 Sedans.  Out of warranty, expect to pay $700+ per door for parts and labor. Some owners had success asking BMW NA to cover all or a portion of the cost for this design defect even when the vehicle was out of warranty.
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          Tail lamp wiring
         </b>
         - The updated E46 sedan (from 9/01 to 3/05 production) wiring harness has a design defect with grounding wires for the rear lighting that are too small and are made of poor quality materials, thus leading to wiring harness failure due to overheating. As stated in BMW's TSB, "Customers may complain that one of the rear lights is inoperative. CAUSE:  Minor corrosion at the 8-pin rear lamp connector creates high resistance causing damage to the connector housing. CORRECTION: Repair the damaged wire(s) and replace damaged connector housing. Install additional ground wires to both left and right rear lamps."  This can be easily confirmed by careful examination of the rear lamp wiring connectors which are usually melted. Symptoms include a "burned out bulb" warning in the instrument panel and (intermittently) completely inoperative rear lamp cluster(s). While BMW has a TSB for this problem, many have occurred out of warranty leading to arguments with the dealer (automotive lighting standards are Federally legislated, yet BMW refuses to repair this design defect once the cars are out of warranty).  BMW dealers expect $350-$400, or more, PER SIDE to make the tail lamps work.  As a result, check for a NHTSA recall (or a class-action lawsuit against BMW) before you pay for repairs.  There are many threads on this problem; see the BMW TIS (search for SIB 63 03 06 if the attached link is inop)
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmwtis.com/tsb/bulletins/bulletin_graphic_temp/B630306g.htm" rel="nofollow">
          here
         </a>
         . This problem was not limited to US market as you can read
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.honestjohn.co.uk/carbycar/index.htm?md=36" rel="nofollow">
          here
         </a>
         .  Cheaper DIY repairs can also be found on a variety of web forums, although your results may vary; here is one:
         <a class="external text" href="http://forums.bimmerforums.com/forum/showthread.php?t=1076114" rel="nofollow">
          here
         </a>
         .
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          Cooling system
         </b>
         - The cooling system will eventually fail catastrophically due to a disintegrating water pump bearing. When this occurs all coolant is lost within seconds and the engine will overheat instantly (remember, these cars have only a total of ~2 gallons of coolant). A much better water pump than the stock/OEM unit is available from EMP Steward, but it's pricey ($200) compared to stock ($70). Other items on the cooling system that should be considered maintenance items since they will likely/eventually fail are the plastic/electric thermostat and the coolant reservoir. Therefore, preventative cooling system maintenance replacing these items every 60k to 80k miles is strongly advised.  If an engine is allowed to seriously overheat the repair costs can reach several thousand dollars because of warped cylinder heads.  There is an excellent write-up on the cooling system and components posted as a sticky on E46fanatics.com written by Mango.
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          VANOS
         </b>
         - Unit wear and failure. This was already the case with the B52 engines in the E36, but it's much easier to repair on the E46's B54 engines since the timing chains do not have to be removed. This defect is mostly related to the Buna o-rings in the unit's control pistons which due to heat induced hardening allow excessive oil bypass, thus leading to less accurate control of camshaft timing. Fluctuating idle or stalling can also be signs of this problem. Depending on maintenance this can already occur at 50K miles. If this defect occurs, there is a noticeable rattle in the engine from the VANOS unit, often around 2,000 rpm and low rpm performance will be affected. Repair is actually relatively easy and a true DIY for someone who has basic skills. Replacing the Buna o-rings with higher quality Viton rings in the VANOS unit will fix the issue. Better yet
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.drvanos.com" rel="nofollow">
          Dr. Vanos
         </a>
         sells complete rebuild and blue printed VANOS units that are even better than new OEM BMW units and
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.beisansystems.com" rel="nofollow">
          Beisan Systems
         </a>
         sells the above mentioned Viton seal/o-ring DIY kits. Cam sensors (intake and exhaust) on the VANOS unit are also prone to fail and as small as they are, they are expensive ($100+). The exhaust sensor is usually the first to fail and that occurs often right around 100K miles. It has been proven that ONLY OEM BMW sensors should be installed during repair since all aftermarket units are not that compatible and of lower quality. VANOS units on ZHP cars are especially failure prone for undetermined reasons. Common opinion is that this is related to the more aggressive camshaft profiles.
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          Subframe
         </b>
         - There are many reports of cracked or torn subframe mounting points. Most often the two rear mounting points below the trunk floor are affected. This occurs more often (but not exclusive to) on the early E46 323/328 models. BMW later improved the subframe mounting points in the trunk floor of the car and in later E46 325i/330i this problem seems to be less common. This problem seems to be so frequent in early E46 cars that a check before buying a 323i/328i IS AN ABSOLUTE MUST! Repairs are very expensive and difficult since the rear axle and subfram have to be removed and the unibody frame and mounting points have to be welded. Recurring stress cracking often occurs even after a repair has been made. You can find more information as well as what it looks like in these threads:
         <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=195602&amp;highlight=subframe" rel="nofollow">
          Thread 1
         </a>
         <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=195600&amp;highlight=frame" rel="nofollow">
          Thread 2
         </a>
         <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=256934&amp;highlight=subframe+video" rel="nofollow">
          Thread 3
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          HVAC
         </b>
         - Many E46 models have erratic HVAC fan speed condition wherein the instrument panel display indicates a set constant fan speed, yet the fan changes speed on a 1hz rate (constantly up and down), or fails to come on at all.  This is almost always results from failure of defective original Final Stage Resistors (FSR) whose design provided insufficient heat sink surface area.  The improved design FSR's can be purchased for ~$60 to $80 from a wide variety of vendors; installation threads abound.
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          Front control arm bushings
         </b>
         -  tend to fail after 40-60k miles.   You can replace them with Powerflex bushings from Bimmerworld for $149 (pre-pressed into new carriers).
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          Ignition Coils
         </b>
         - There was a recall for failure-prone Bremi ignition coils.  Symptoms include multiple yet intermittent "cylinder misfire" OBD-II codes, among with other difficult to diagnose problems.  A dealer can tell you if this TSB/recall has been performed in which all six Bremi coils were replaced.  The following build date &amp; VIN ranges were affected by this recall:
        </li>
       </ul>
       <div style="border-left: 0.2em solid #3CABB2; margin-left: 0.5em; padding-left: 0.5em;">
        <ul>
         <li>
          E46 with M54/M56 from 09/02 up to 12/04 production date.
         </li>
         <li>
          325i KL58793  KL62880, NH02298  NH05784, PD00558  PD01068
         </li>
         <li>
          325iA KL78812  KL89995, KR24002  KR32361, PD56824  PD58282, NJ21783  NJ47934, NJ80013  NJ96910
         </li>
         <li>
          325Ci JY96097  JY98108, PC99012  PC99995
         </li>
         <li>
          325CiA PL00001  PL04548, PG60108  PG62814
         </li>
         <li>
          325Cic JY43694  JY44229, PG97089  PG98243
         </li>
         <li>
          325CicA PG88872  PG92999, PL24020  PL31534
         </li>
         <li>
          325iT EZ15376  EZ15633
         </li>
         <li>
          325iTA PC11346  PC12725
         </li>
         <li>
          325xi PF58422  PF62576
         </li>
         <li>
          325xiA PH86839  PH90969, PM52033  PM59296, PR06010  PR12874
         </li>
         <li>
          325xiT PE91490  PE92062
         </li>
         <li>
          325xiTA PF01600  PF04589
         </li>
         <li>
          325iA SULEV KP78010  KP87556, PH30108  PH36104
         </li>
         <li>
          325CiA SULEV PJ15045  PJ16347, JT20009  JT22530
         </li>
         <li>
          325iTA SULEV PJ00063  PJ00924
         </li>
         <li>
          330i KM02321  KM07066
         </li>
         <li>
          330iA KM24352  KM36386
         </li>
         <li>
          330Ci PD95092  PD97653, JU28717  JU45159
         </li>
         <li>
          330CiA PL10037  PL14136, PH02210  PH05245
         </li>
         <li>
          330Cic EV90090  EV90753, PJ94042  PJ95840
         </li>
         <li>
          330CicA JU95942  JU99831, PL40018  PL46594
         </li>
         <li>
          330xi PG09391  PG11594
         </li>
         <li>
          330xiA PG20116  PG23990, PN30039  PN35923
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <ul>
        <li>
         <b>
          FM Stereo
         </b>
         - There was a technical service bulletin for fading FM stereo reception on cars with navigation with the BM53 tuner.  The fix is to replace the BM53 tuner in the trunk.  Reference service measure #B65-209-04 with your dealer.
        </li>
        <li>
         There was a technical service bulletin for a 4000RPM power dip on cars equipped with the ZHP Performance Package.   The fix is to send the car's DME to New Jersey for reprogramming.  Reference service bulletin # SIB 12 17 05 with your dealer - More info here:
         <a class="external free" href="http://www.linquist.net/motorsports/bmw/sib121705.txt" rel="nofollow">
          http://www.linquist.net/motorsports/bmw/sib121705.txt
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          Radiator Cooling Fan
         </b>
         - There was a recall of the electric radiator cooling fan on a wide variety of BMW models, to include many early E46's. The problem could result in an engine compartment electrical fire several minutes after the engine was shut off.  Several cars (and homes) were destroyed by the resulting fires.
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          Sunroof
         </b>
         - The sunroof shade track/rails are prone to failure.  The sunroof will sometimes fail to operate in the heat on older models.
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          Weather Stripping
         </b>
         - The interior weather stripping above the coupe doors often falls down after a few years.  Easily glued into place.  (Some even fell down before the cars were sold new.)
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          Erratic Idle
         </b>
         - There was a technical service bulletin for an erratic idle with possible stalling.  Reference service measure #B12-207-0 with your dealer.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Is_the_330.2F328_worth_the_price_premium_over_the_325.2F323.3F">
         Is the 330/328 worth the price premium over the 325/323?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Nobody can answer this question but you.  The 330/328 obviously have more hp and torque, as well as bigger brakes.  To make the 330/328 a better
        <i>
         value
        </i>
        , BMW includes more options as standard with the "up level" model (such as power seats, HK premium sound in later years, trip computer, etc.).  Furthermore, there would likely be a premium back when you sell or trade it in. In covertible version the differences are even more pronounced since the convertible is a much heavier car and the substantially higher torque of the 328/330 engines are very helpful. Fuel economy is surprisingly identical between the engines since the smaller engines have to be pushed harder in traffic what the larger engines accomplish with more ease. Test drive a car in your price range and see if it meets your needs.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Should_I_buy_the_extended_maintenance_or_extended_warranty.3F">
         Should I buy the extended maintenance or extended warranty?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        First of all, you should recognize the difference between maintenance and warranty.  BMW offered 36,000 mi/3yr or 50,000 mi/4yr free maintenance (depending on year).  This maintenance covered oil changes, brakes, and windshield wipers (it may also cover items like coolant or brake fluid flush depending on timing).   BMW also offered a 50,000 mi/4yr bumper to bumper warranty, which covers any problems you may have.
       </p>
       <p>
        <b>
         If your car has &lt;50,000 miles
        </b>
        , then you can extend the free maintenance to 100,000 mi/6yr.   This extension can be purchased from any BMW dealer and the maintenance can be performed by any dealer.  There are deals out there where dealers are offering the maintenance extension for as low as $950.   A single 4-wheel brake job can cost about that much if performed by a dealer.  Additionally, worn clutch replacements are included within the extended maintenance plan.
        <b>
         If you are comfortable doing your own work, it's rarely worth extending the maintenance.
        </b>
       </p>
       <p>
        BMW offers two types of warranty extensions:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Certified Pre-Owned warranty:  The CPO warranty covers you until 6yrs/100k miles from the original in-service date.  It covers most of the drivetrain, but NOT most of the electronics.  This is generally offered on pre-owned cars sold by a BMW dealer.
        </li>
        <li>
         BMW Original Owner Protection Coverage (2OP):  This is offered to the original owner or lessee only and can only be purchased while the car is still under the original 4yr/50k mile factory warranty.  Its coverage is identical to that of the CPO warranty.  More information on this warranty can be found
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/attachment.php?attachmentid=99404&amp;d=1172689549" rel="nofollow">
          here
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        Any other warranty offered to you will be underwritten by a third party.
       </p>
       <div style="border-left: 0.2em solid red; margin-left: 0.5em; padding-left: 0.5em;">
        <p>
         Here on Bimmerfest, many of us are proponents of underwriting your own warranty!   Take the $2000 that an extended warranty would typically cost you and stick it into an interest bearing account.   Find a good independent BMW mechanic and pay for any repairs that come up out of that account.    I can almost guarantee that at the end of the "would be" warranty period, you'll have money in that account left over!
        </p>
       </div>
       <p>
        Here's a small FAQ on
        <i>
         third party
        </i>
        extended warranties:
       </p>
       <div style="border-left: 0.2em solid #3CABB2; margin-left: 0.5em; padding-left: 0.5em;">
        <p>
         <b>
          How much does the extended warranty cost? Is the price negotiable?
         </b>
         "Service contracts" vary in price according to length and level of coverage, as well as by "deductible." Most definitely, the price is negotiable. The cost of the service contract is also dependent on who the provider is, and how likely they are to be in business in a few years. NOTE:  These policies are either "Named Component" or "Named Exclusion" programs.  The difference is that the latter is far better.  In a Named Component program, ONLY the items listed in your contract are covered.  In a Named Exclusion program everything is covered, except for the specific items listed in your contract.  One of the major ways these programs can deny coverage is when an esoteric component fails, and it is not listed in a Named Component program.  Hence, if you feel you must buy one of these contracts (which have very large markups), then get a Named Exclusion policy.
        </p>
        <p>
         <b>
          Can I buy the policy through any dealer or only from the dealer that I bought the car from?
         </b>
         Most service contracts can be purchased from any dealer. Some dealerships are signed up with specific warranty providers that will not permit a warranty to be placed on a vehicle that was not serviced and sold through the dealership.
        </p>
        <p>
         <b>
          Can I get repairs done at any dealer in the country?
         </b>
         Generally speaking, the repair doesn't even have to be performed by a "dealer" per se... The only requirement (in most cases) is that the repair is performed by a reputable licensed repair facility... As a general rule, "deductibles" are usually lower, or are waived if the repair is performed by the selling dealer.
        </p>
        <p>
         <b>
          Is the policy underwritten by a 3rd party or BMW?
         </b>
         Unfortunately, service contracts for BMW's are only (at this time) administered by a 3rd party...:-(
        </p>
        <p>
         <b>
          What happens if this third party company goes bankrupt, does the dealership take over the policy?
         </b>
         Unfortunately, no... If the company goes bankrupt, you will probably lose your money... This has happened before. Make sure that you select a solid one.
As long as you purchase a warranty from an insured provider you will be fine. There are many to choose from and they are affordable.
        </p>
        <p>
         <b>
          How long do you have after buying the car to decide on buying the extended warranty?
         </b>
         You have up until there is a minmum of 1 month, *and* 1,000 miles remaining on the original factory warranty...
        </p>
        <p>
         <b>
          Is the only variable between buying the policy now instead of at the end of the allowable period the possibility that the price of the policy might go up? If so, how much have prices been going up recently.
         </b>
         The advantage of getting one early is obviously financial... If you buy one with the car, the cost can be included (i.e. financed) right in with the rest of the deal, and included in your monthly payments. There is also the issue of an "eligibility surcharge" that gets applied at various levels or intervals... Lastly, they do go up in price regularly... The last price increase I saw was on the order of several hundred dollars... Because service contracts are "transferable", and build "future value" it may make sense for some buyers to get one. If you are going to get one, the sooner the better... One thing is a given fact: they will go up in price... Think of them as a hedge against inflation. "Lock-in" future repairs at today's costs...
        </p>
       </div>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="What_are_the_car.2Fkey_memory_options.3F">
         What are the car/key memory options?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        They can be set by a dealer or any independent mechanic with a MODIC3/GT1 BMW diagnostic computer.
       </p>
       <p>
        The list of programmable options can be found here.
        <a class="external free" href="http://www.ge39.com/files/BMW_MemoryOptions.pdf" rel="nofollow">
         http://www.ge39.com/files/BMW_MemoryOptions.pdf
        </a>
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Options_.26_Package_Codes">
         Options &amp; Package Codes
        </span>
       </h3>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Summary">
         Summary
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        BMW of North America offers specific option packages.  Elsewhere in the world, a program called BMW Individual is offered to allow individuals to better mix and match options.  Options and packages often have numerical or alphanumerical codes associated with them.  These codes are used as shorthand to describe the option or package on many BMW forums around the internet.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Option_codes">
         Option codes
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showpost.php?p=1199505&amp;postcount=1" rel="nofollow">
         Here
        </a>
        is a list of option codes in a post by Terry Kennedy.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Option_packages">
         Option packages
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        This information is specific to US-bound E46s.
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="ZSP_-_Sport_Package">
         ZSP - Sport Package
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        The sport package has been available on all E46 3-series cars.  It typically included:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         A 3-spoke multifunction steering wheel
        </li>
        <li>
         Sport seats with adjustable thigh support and heavier, more pronounced side bolsters.
        </li>
        <li>
         Sport wheels and tires (larger wheels with a different design and lower-profile tires)
        </li>
        <li>
         Sport suspension calibration (stiffer springs/shocks).  Note that 2001 and up 330i sedans got the sport suspension as standard equipment that all Coupes recieved.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="ZPP_-_Premium_Package">
         ZPP - Premium Package
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        The premium package has been available on all 3-series cars.  It typically included:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Different wheels/tires [if ordered with the sport package, the sport package wheels/tires superseed]
        </li>
        <li>
         A multifunction steering wheel [IF it was not already standard on the vehicle]
        </li>
        <li>
         Wood grain interior trim [if ordered with the sport package, the premium package wood is typically installed, unless specifically requested otherwise]
        </li>
        <li>
         Rain-sensing windshield wipers (became standard equipment in 2004)
        </li>
        <li>
         Auto-dimming rear-view mirror
        </li>
        <li>
         Power seats
        </li>
        <li>
         Lumbar Support (not available on the 325)
        </li>
        <li>
         Moonroof (note: moonroof can also be ordered separately)
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="ZHP_-_Performance_Package">
         ZHP - Performance Package
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        The performance package was available on 2003-2005 330 sedans (330i) and 2004-2006 330 coupes and convertibles (330Ci/330Cic). In 2003, it was only available with the 6-speed manual transmission and WITHOUT the premium package. In 2004, all performance package cars were also available with the automatic (steptronic) transmission as well as the premium package.
       </p>
       <p>
        Obviously, the Performance Package is an inclusive optional package incorporating all of the features of the Sport Package, so they're not available together.
       </p>
       <p>
        Original Press release:  The 330i Performance Package has been created exclusively for the U.S. market for enthusiasts by enthusiasts at BMW Individual, a division of BMW M GmbH. There is no aspect of the driving experience that has not been enhanced by the Performance Package. Modifications to the 3.0-liter in-line six-cylinder engine, which include different camshafts and performance-modified Digital Motor Electronics, yield a ten horsepower increase to 235. For the first time in a 330i a six-speed manual transmission will be standard. With the Performance Package it will include a short-throw shifter. The package also includes a shorter final drive ratio. The benefits of these modifications are immediately apparent - the 330i with a Performance Package will accelerate from 0 - 60 miles-per-hour in 6 seconds, about half a second faster than a standard 330i. To match the straight-line performance a new sports suspension, more aggressively tuned than the 330i's standard sport suspension, is mated to 18-inch wheels with mixed-size performance tires. In addition to the wheels and tires the exterior of the 330i Performance Package is distinguished by its Aerodynamic Package, black headlight trim, high gloss shadowline trim and a new exhaust that not only appears but also sounds more aggressive. The look and feel of the interior has been refined with cloth and Alcantara sport seats matching the Alcantara sport steering wheel. An anthracite headliner and Black cube aluminum trim complete an ambiance tailored to the enthusiast. Silver cube aluminum trim is optional. The instrumentation includes red needles while the tachometer reflects the modified engine's 300 higher rpm limit. Production of the 330i Performance Package will begin in March 2003 with the first cars arriving at BMW centers in April.
       </p>
       <p>
        TEXT COURTESY of BMWNA
       </p>
       <p>
        Per the BMW press release, this package included the following changes. However, many of these claims have been found to be misleading:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Engine mods that equal a gain of 10HP &amp; 8 ft/lb of torque by reprogramming the Digital Motor Electronics to allow a 6800 RPM max (up from 6500).
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         6 speed short throw shifter (for manual transmission equipped cars)
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         3.07:1 Final drive ratio w/ manual trans instead of the standard 2.91:1. Convertibles retained the already installed 3.07 ratio.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Max Speed Limiter set to 155 mph (instead of 128)
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         New M suspension, more "sporty" than standard or poor road package.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        There are no "ZHP" specific springs. The same springs are used for comparably equipped 330's for both the ZSP and the ZHP. In both cases, 
the spring rate for the post 4/01 build ZSP and ZHP is believed to be slightly less than that of the pre-4/01 ZSP
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Firmer shocks (Jounce: front +50%, rear +20%), (Rebound: front +35%, rear -8%)
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        ZHP does use different dampers than the ZSP. There is a shortage of shock dyno data, but based on the SACHS damping parameter values it is believe 
the jounce damping is the same but rebound damping is stiffer on the ZHP. Pre-4/01 sport package cars had similar damping values to the ZHP but 
used the higher grade SACHS "Advantage" dampers rather than the "Super Touring" model.
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Smaller diameter anti-roll bars: 23.5 mm front (v. 24mm pre-04/01 ZSP), 18mm rear (v. 19mm pre-04/01 ZSP)
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        There is no 18.5 mm rear sway bar offered by BMW for the E46.
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         More rigid forward bushings
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        Front Control arm bushings are the same ZHP/ZSP
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         ZHP control arms are different and use a stiffer ball joint
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Lower ride height by 15 mm (.6 inches) utilizing shorter auxiliary springs
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        Since both the ZSP and ZHP use the same springs, they have the same ride height. Both are 15mm lower than a non-sport E46 
-.5 degrees of camber (for a total of -1.1 degrees)
Alignment settings are the same ZSP and ZHP
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Exterior trim elements (front &amp; rear fascia, trunk lid spoiler)
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Special exterior trim: Anthracite (charcoal) headlight surrounds, High-Gloss
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Shadowline (black gloss) trim
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Large diameter stainless steel dual exhaust outlets
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Extra thick Alcantara steering wheel (later switched to perforated leather)
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         ZSP Sport Seats
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Alcantara &amp; cloth upholstery to replace leatherette and standard trim (leather still optional)
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Choice of "Black Cube" or "Silver Cube" interior trim
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Red needles on the instrument cluster
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Style 135's are added, 18x8.0" front, 18x8.5" rear
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Wider Tires: 225/40ZR-18 in front and 255/35ZR-18 in the rear.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Reduced steering rack ratio. 13.7:1 versus 15.5:1
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        All post 4/01 330's use the same ratio steering rack. The ratio of this rack is 13.7:1, it is believed to be different from that used on the 325's
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="ZCP_-_Competition_Package">
         ZCP - Competition Package
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        The Competition Package was offered on 2005-2006 M3 coupes only. It included:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Interlagos Blue as a color option
        </li>
        <li>
         Larger compound/cross-drilled brakes, with larger rear piston and special brake pads. Same as CSL
        </li>
        <li>
         M-Track mode DSC (a traction control mode that allows for more 'playing')
        </li>
        <li>
         Alcantara M3 steering wheel (audio and cruise control buttons deleted) and Alcantara e-brake handle
        </li>
        <li>
         19" BBS "cross-spoke" design wheels 19"x 8" front/ 19"x 9.5" rear
        </li>
        <li>
         Shorter ratio steering rack. 14.5:1 versus 15.4:1. Same as CSL
        </li>
        <li>
         Aluminum "Alu Tec" interior trim
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="ZCW_-_Cold_weather_package">
         ZCW - Cold weather package
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        The cold weather package has been available on all 3-series and M3 cars.  It typically included:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Pass-through ski bag
        </li>
        <li>
         Heated seats
        </li>
        <li>
         Headlight washers
        </li>
       </ul>

        <span class="mw-headline" id="Check_Engine.2FService_Engine_Soon_Light_.28CEL.2FSES.29_scanning_for_ERROR_CODES">

        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/wiki/index.php/BMW_E46#Engine" rel="nofollow">

       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_service">
         Oil service
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Although BMW recommends oil service every 15,000 miles, the majority of forum members perform them at half the interval - every 7500 miles.    Oil and filter change info can be found on
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.my330i.com/lof.php" rel="nofollow">
         My330i.com here
        </a>
        .  
Paul180 also has a great DIY
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmw330ci.net/maintenance/oil.php" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .  You can also use an Oil Extractor (Pela makes popular models) to perform the oil change, link 1 is
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmw325i.net/maint_oil_extractor.shtml" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        and link 2
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=387408&amp;highlight=" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .  There are concerns that an improper oil filter change can lead to leaks at the oil filter housing gasket.  See the oil filter housing section under other maintenance for further insight.
       </p>
       <p>
        You can purchase
        <a href="/wiki/index.php/OEM" title="OEM">
         OEM
        </a>
        (Mann brand) filters for under $5 online on sites like
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.autohausaz.com/index.html" rel="nofollow">
         Autohaus Arizona
        </a>
        or
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.ecstuning.com/BMW-E46-330i-M54_3.0L/Maintenance/Engine/Oil_Filter/" rel="nofollow">
         ECS Tuning
        </a>
        .   If you drive a BMW in the USA, you should always use an oil that meets BMW's LL-01 specification.  BMW's LL-04 spec is only approved for non-USA vehicles, and this is due to the formula inconsistencies and high sulfur content of many USA gasolines.
       </p>
       <p>
        That limits USA drivers to either:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         BMW's own "High Performance SAE 5W-30 Synthetic Oil"
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>

           </a>
          </li>

           </a>

       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Resetting_the_service_indicator">
         Resetting the service indicator
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        The service indicator toggles between "Oil service" and "Inspection", and when reset, begins counting down from approximately 15,000 miles.  It gets to zero miles once your car has consumed 2500L of fuel.
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Model_Year_1999_to_Mid-2000">
         Model Year 1999 to Mid-2000
        </span>
       </h5>
       <ol>
        <li>
         Locate the 20-pin OBD connector.  It is under the hood, passenger side, behind the battery terminal.
        </li>
        <li>
         Open the connector, and locate pins 7 and 19. The connector has a pacman in the center, surrounded by two rings of pins.  Pin 7 is on the outer ring opposite the pacman's mouth.  Pin 19 is on the inner ring 90 degrees clockwise from pin 7. If you don't know where these are, follow the link to pictures below.
        </li>
        <li>
         Turn the ignition switch to position 2 (RUN), but not to start - notice that this is different than the process used in slightly older cars.
        </li>
        <li>
         Connect together pins 7 and 19 for about 5 seconds, then remove the jumper.
         <ul>
          <li>
           <b>
            WARNING
           </b>
           - Do not keep the jumper in place longer - if you get to 10 seconds you will reset the Inspection I/II Indicator. (unless of course that is what you are trying to do!)
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
        <li>
         Turn off the ignition key.
        </li>
       </ol>
       <p>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmwe36blog.com/2007/02/24/reset-bmw-e36-oil-service-light/" rel="nofollow">
         Photos detailing the procedure can be found here.
        </a>
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="After_Mid-2000">
         After Mid-2000
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        You should not have the 20-pin DLC connector. You only need to HOLD the left odometer reset button WHILE turning the key to position 1 (Accessory). Keep holding the button for 5 or so seconds until any of the following shows in the display: OIL SERVICE or INSPECTION with RESET or RE. Release the button and press it again for another 5 or so seconds until RESET or RE flash. While the display flashes, press the button one more time briefly. If done correctly, END SIA should show up for a few seconds. All done.
       </p>
       <p>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2K8AF-vuL8E" rel="nofollow">
         Here is a video on how to reset the indicator.
        </a>
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Inspection_I_.2F_Inspection_II">
         Inspection I / Inspection II
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Inspection I should be performed at 30,000, 90,000, and 150,000 miles.  Inspection II should be performed at 60,000, 120,000, and 180,000 miles.
       </p>
       <p>
        For a high level overview of what is included in Inspection I and II, go
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerzone.com/inspection.htm" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        To get started on many of the Inspection II items that are simply 'inspections' of various parts throughout the vehicle, see the three inspection guides posted
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?p=4393590#post4393590" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        <b>
         EPBB
        </b>
        has written up some great Inspection I/Inspection II instructions that guide you through some of the actual maintenance tasks that you should perform, you can find those
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=109846" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Transmission_fluid">
         Transmission fluid
        </span>
       </h3>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Automatic_Transmission">
         Automatic Transmission
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/attachment.php?attachmentid=119548&amp;d=1188433844" rel="nofollow">
         Here
        </a>
        is a service bulletin on how to check your ATF fluid.
       </p>
       <p>
        <br/>
        Bimmerfest user
        <b>
         Torquewrench
        </b>
        wrote an
        <i>
         awesome
        </i>
        how-to on changing your automatic transmission fluid (Esso ATF LT71141) &amp; filter on a ZF auto transmission
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=166135" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        :
       </p>
       <p>
        For the green stickered GM-France built 5L40-E/GM5 (A5S 390R); BMW specifies replacement fill as Texaco ETL 8072-B. It is available in 25 liter bulk containers for about $180 from mileoneparts.com (BMW p/n 83-22-0-403-249)
       </p>
       <p>
        ATF (ETL 8072B, GM transmission) change DIY by Starless (bimmerfest.com) can be found
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=443800" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        Texaco USA does not stock that product in one liter bottles. I emailed them (Texaco) and they recommended using Havoline Multi-Vehicle ATF.
       </p>
       <p>
        Havoline's corporate product data sheet cites Havoline Multi-Vehicle ATF as a suitable replacement fill for both ETL 8072-B and ETL 7045-E (used on the ZF trans).   A local Havoline distributor will drop ship a box of 12 ea. one (1) quart bottles for about $50.  gordo325xiwagon Aug07
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Manual_Transmission">
         Manual Transmission
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        impee.co.uk has an excellent tutorial on changing manual transmission fluid
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.impee.co.uk/transmission_fluid_change.htm" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .  Tim330i at diymybmw.com also has one
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.diymybmw.com/e46/manual-transmission-fluid-change/" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .  For the M3, M3.MADRUSSIAN.NET has
        <a class="external text" href="http://m3.madrussian.net/diy_rp_tranny_fluid.shtml" rel="nofollow">
         this
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        Many suggest Redline MTL or D4 ATF in the manual transmission.  Some recommend sticking with
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=80844" rel="nofollow">
         BMW MTF-LT-2
        </a>
        **Ok to substitute Pentosin 1028AMZ0632 MTF2 (75W-80 GL-4 in 1 liter containers for $18.50 at pelicanparts.com) in place of Lifetime Oil MTF-LT-2(BMW part #: 83-22-0-309-031 5 liter container for $128) Pentosin is the OEM supplier for this fluid.**  E46 AWD models' transfer cases use the same fluid type as the transmission.
       </p>
       <p>
        Castrol VMX80 is also 75W80 GL-4, and since BMW fluids are often rebranded Castrol, there is speculation that it's the same.  Unconfirmed as of yet.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Differential_fluid">
         Differential fluid
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        bokchoys.com has a good tutorial on changing your differential fluid
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bokchoys.com/differential/diff_fluid.htm" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        . impee.co.uk has a similar one with additional photos
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.impee.co.uk/bmw_differential_oil.htm" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .  There is a discrepancy in torque specs between the two tutorials.  TIS service instructions from 2005 state that drain plugs with the rubber o-ring should be tightened to 44 ft-lbs/60Nm; drain plugs with the metal seal should be tightened to 48 ft-lbs/65Nm.
       </p>
       <p>
        Many do-it-yourselfers use Redline or Amsoil 75W-90 GL-5 hypoid gear oil.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Brakes">
         Brakes
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Please refer to
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/wiki/index.php/BMW_E46#Brakes_2" rel="nofollow">
         the Brakes Section
        </a>
        of this Wiki for brake options and maintenance information.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Coolant">
         Coolant
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Thanks to Paul180, a great DIY can be found
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmw330ci.net/maintenance/coolant.php" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        . BMW recommends using only BMW-approved coolants, but many people have used other brands and have noticed absolutely no difference in performance of the coolant or the car. For a detailed explanation of different coolant types, watch this
        <a class="external text" href="http://youtu.be/LrpLRSWE-ZY" rel="nofollow">
         video
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        Some feel modern coolants are most likely the same in composition, and pre-mixed 50/50 brands that are sold locally are very good coolants. Some of the most important characteristics of a good coolant are its pH, boiling point, and freezing point. The common coolants perform very well in those three areas.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Spark_Plugs">
         Spark Plugs
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Please see these threads:
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=213711" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 1 (Newer coil design)
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/archive/index.php/t-65380.html" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 2 (Older coil design)
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        Paul180 also has a DIY that covers spark plugs and the valve cover gasket.  Check it out
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmw330ci.net/maintenance/valve.php" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        Sidefly has a DIY for his 2001 325Ci
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.e46fanatics.com/pdf/2001_325Ci_E46_Valve_Cover_Replacement.pdf" rel="nofollow">
         available here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        Consider using Permatex Hylomar Universal Blue Racing Formula Gasket Dressing &amp; Flange Sealant wherever 3 Bond Sealant is required (valve cover gasket half moon shaped areas, oil pan gasket flanges etc. - since 3 Bond Sealant is not readily available)
       </p>
       <p>
        Solidjake has a DIY VIDEO for his 2002 330i spark plugs and spark plug boots.
        <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=383761" rel="nofollow">
         [2]
        </a>
        <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=411056" rel="nofollow">
         [3]
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        It is strongly recommended to ONLY use the OEM specified NGK plugs for replacements. Bosch Platinum 4 plugs are also available for the M54 engine but will often not perform, cause misfires and set CEL light and codes. Better stick with the NGKs even though they are more expensive.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Cabin_Microfilter_replacement">
         Cabin Microfilter replacement
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        It takes all of 30 seconds, and no tools; why pay the dealer to do this?  Paul180 has a good DIY
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmw330ci.net/maintenance/cabinfilter.php" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel_filter_replacement_.26_Fuel_Pump_Diagnosis_and_Replacement">
         Fuel filter replacement &amp; Fuel Pump Diagnosis and Replacement
        </span>
       </h3>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Filter">
         Filter
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        Please see
        <a class="external text" href="http://bimmerinfo.com/diy/fuel-filter/" rel="nofollow">
         this page
        </a>
        at Bimmerinfo.com.
Paul180 also has a DIY
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmw330ci.net/maintenance/fuelfilter.php" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        While BMW considers the fuel filter to be a "lifetime" part which never requires replacement, replacement is relatively cheap insurance against premature fuel pump failure.  One US member reported that his filter was nearly clogged at 60k miles (as suggested by an inability to blow through the old filter).  In contrast, the new filter had no resistance (akin to blowing through a straw).  Look at the fuel color and contents of Solidjake's 88,000 mile old fuel filter after replacement
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=393302&amp;highlight=" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Pump">
         Pump
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        Here's a youtube video on the diagnose and replace process:
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aqVGpkan0rE" rel="nofollow">
         click here
        </a>
        Best to have a near-empty tank of gas if you can before you pull the pump to minimize fuel spillage.
       </p>
       <p>
        Pumps usually last 6-12 years and can fail due to time as much as miles.  Many replace preventively at 10 years or before 150k miles.  Running gas of questionable quality and running below 1/4 tank frequently may shorten the life of the pump due to increased contaminants and lack of fuel quantity needed to keep the pump running cool.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Engine_drive_belt_chirping.2Fcracking.2Freplacement">
         Engine drive belt chirping/cracking/replacement
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        If the main drive belt ("serpentine belt") is making noise, it may be worn, but most likely one of your idler or tensioner pulleys has worn out and is squawking as it turns.  It tends to be most noticeable on cold starts in the winter.  See the Cooling section below regarding diagnostic/replacement of these pulleys.  Cracks- a serpentine belt with a few cracks here and there is ok, but when you see more than a few in a 1-2" section, it's ready to be replaced.
       </p>
       <p>
        See Paul180's replacement DIY
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmw330ci.net/maintenance/belts.php" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
