       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Where_can_I_find_switched_power_.28.2B12v.29_for_accessories.3F">
         Where can I find switched power (+12v) for accessories?
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Three places:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         BMW offers a 12v accessory power cable that plugs into the torch charger in the glove compartment (But is not switched power).
        </li>
        <li>
         There's a wiring harness in the headliner console that has +12v for the universal garage door opener (UGDO).  It's usually wrapped in black tape and shoved up above the passenger visor area.  The +12v wire is green &amp; blue.
        </li>
        <li>
         There's a wiring harness in the center console under the coin tray for the analog cellular telephone option.  The +12v wire is purple/white.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        Ground is always brown.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Want_to_put_your_convertible_top_up.2Fdown_with_the_key.3F">
         Want to put your convertible top up/down with the key?
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Check out
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=483072" rel="nofollow">
         this great how-to
        </a>
        over on e46fanatics.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Troubleshooting">
         Troubleshooting
        </span>
       </h3>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Turn_signal_bulb_burned_out.3F">
         Turn signal bulb burned out?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=223928" rel="nofollow">
         Here
        </a>
        is a DIY on changing your front turn signal bulb.
       </p>
       <p>
        <a class="external text" href="http://m3.madrussian.net/diy_front_turnsignal.shtml" rel="nofollow">
         This
        </a>
        is also another good reference for pre-facelift cars.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Tail_light_ground_recall.2FDoes_your_car_think_you_have_a_tail_light_out_when_you_have_no_burned_out_bulbs.3F">
         Tail light ground recall/Does your car think you have a tail light out when you have no burned out bulbs?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        First, consider replacing any dark or discolored bulbs with known good bulbs, preferably of the same brand.  (However, this is unlikely to solve the problem for long, if at all.  Here's why:  accessing the bulbs results in moving or josting the wiring.  This can make it seem like you've solved the problem, when the problem actually lies within the wiring connections--it is very likely to return.)
       </p>
       <p>
        Second, examine your tail lamp wiring connectors for evidence of internal overheating.  See the instructions in BMW S IB (service bulletin) 63 03 06
        <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.bmwtis.com/tsb/bulletins/bulletin_graphic_temp/B630306g.htm" rel="nofollow">
         [14]
        </a>
        .  Print this out for your BMW Center if the car is still under any warranty.  The bulletin directs replacement of the melted wiring and connectors, and creates a second, more robust, grounding path for both tail lamp assemblies.  NOTE:  BMW Dealers have been asking $600 to $800+ to repair this known wiring defect.  Defects which prevent automotive lighting from meeting FMVSS 108 are subject to recall for a period of at least ten years, and frequently much longer due to liability issues [see
        <a class="external free" href="http://fmvss108.tripod.com/" rel="nofollow">
         http://fmvss108.tripod.com/
        </a>
        for details on the applicable Federal Motor Vehicle Lighting Standard].  From the NHTSA web site:  "Safety recall campaigns result from identified component failures which present a risk to highway safety, and from non-compliance with Federal Motor Vehicle Safety Standards.  Although a majority of safety recalls are performed by manufacturers without any influence from NHTSA, many result from NHTSA defect investigations and compliance testing."
       </p>
       <p>
        On 8/7/09, NHTSA opened an investigation of tail lamp electrical connection (ground circuit) issues for all MY 2002 - 2005 E46 sedans.  On 12/18/09, NHTSA elevated their investigation to an "engineering analysis" (EA09-019). This investigation is ongoing and NHTSA laboratory investigations of the 'alleged' defect, and a report are expected by June 30, 2010. Interested parties may access the details of this investigation and NHTSA, BMW correspondence by going to NHTSA's web site: "defect investigations."
       </p>
       <p>
        If you elect to pay for the repair in advance of the recall and/or clas action lawsuit, SAVE ALL RELATED RECEIPTS.  You may need receipt copies for full reimbursement from BMW.
       </p>
       <p>
        On 9/04/2011, NHTSA announced a recall of MY 2002 - 2005 325i, 325xi, 330i, 330xi models built between 9/01/2001 and 3/01/2005 to repair the open ground connection at the 8-pin connnector of the tail light assembly. A total of 241,000 vehicles are affected.  The recall identification number is 11V438000.  Repairs will be made free of charge.  Owner notification is expected to begin in October of 2011.  Owner's may Google 'NHTSA Recalls' and enter the appropriate model information to view documents as BMW submits them to NHTSA.
       </p>
       <p>
        <b>
         DIY Repair -
        </b>
        If you think you have this problem but are outside the coverage dates,
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=512469" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        is a thread on the very simple DIY repair.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Electrical_systems_going_whack.3F_.28Dying_Battery_or_Failed_iBus_device.29">
         Electrical systems going whack? (Dying Battery or Failed iBus device)
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        There are two problems that affect all of your electrical systems.  Symptoms include steering wheel buttons not working, turn signals or gauges not working, radio not turning on, etc.
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         The most common cause is a failed device on the iBus: try unplugging your cd changer, ipod adapter, satellite radio, etc.
        </li>
        <li>
         The second most common cause is simply a bad battery.  Batteries on the E46 are known to only last about four years.  Using the Hidden Onboard Computer Functions directions above, you can monitor your system voltage.  A healthy battery will show around 12 volts with the car off, and around 14 volts while running.  A cheaper than OEM replacement battery is the "49DL" available from autozone.  Although this battery is of different size and dimension of the OEM battery it can be made to fit and functions properly.  Here's a thread with some details:
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=162476" rel="nofollow">
          Thread 1
         </a>
         . Many festers have also had luck with an Everstart MAXX 94R or RN found at Walmart, which is the correct original size and dimensions as the OEM battery. You can read the details in this thread:
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=417105" rel="nofollow">
          Thread 2
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Convertibles have a smaller battery tray in the trunk and are unable to use the 49DL and must use the 94R sized battery.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        "49DL" and "94R" are standardized battery sizes that will have specific height, width, and length dimensions.  See the threads above for further information.
       </p>
       <p>
        <br/>
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         If your battery dies and you successfully charge it and restart the car only to find many electrical accessories not working, a    "hard" reset of the system may be necessary.  This involves removing both battery cables and then shorting them together (NOT the terminal posts on the battery!!!) for up to 30 minutes.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         If you believe your battery and alternator are good, but the battery keeps dying, you may have what is called a parasitic drain - some electrical component stays on when it's not supposed to and drains the battery when the car's not running.  See this thread for troubleshooting:
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=694213" rel="nofollow">
          Thread 1
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        The wiring harness to the trunk may also deteriorate over time/use and cause multiple shorts, resulting in the "christmas tree" of lights on the dash and other erratic electrical behavior.  See the sticky thread at the top of the e46 forum on this with discussion of remedies.
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         <b>
          Instrument cluster malfunctioning?
         </b>
         See OBC computer section above for the cluster test and OBC system reset functions, menu options #2 and #21.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Problems_Starting_with_possible_other_odd_electrical_behavior">
         Problems Starting with possible other odd electrical behavior
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        See
        <b>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=596758" rel="nofollow">
          this thread
         </a>
        </b>
        for symptoms and
        <b>
         ignition switch replacement DIY
        </b>
        .  Problems with the ignition switch are usually characterized by the starter not engaging every time the key is turned and/or a long delay between turning the key to the start position and the starter actually engaging.  Note: starting problems can also be associated with a weak/dead battery (see above in Electrical), fuel/spark problems and/or problems with the starter itself (See
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/wiki/index.php/BMW_E46#No_Start" rel="nofollow">
         No Start
        </a>
        under Engine/Troubleshooting below).
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Remote_lock.2Funlock_on_your_key_not_working.3F">
         Remote lock/unlock on your key not working?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Try re-initializing your key:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Get in and close all doors.
        </li>
        <li>
         Turn on the ignition and turn off quickly. (No more than 5 seconds) to start the process. Next action must take place within 30 seconds.
        </li>
        <li>
         Remove the 1st key.
        </li>
        <li>
         Hold the key up near your left shoulder (this is so it is closer to the remote reciever antenna - someone else suggested this).
        </li>
        <li>
         Hold down the unlock button (which is button 1 on my key) and press the lock button 3 times (center button on my key). Release the unlock button and the doors lock which confirms the operation.
        </li>
        <li>
         Quickly repeat steps 4 &amp; 5 for key #2 etc.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        If it does not work, try doing the keys in opposite order. Key 2 then key1, vs 1 then 2.
       </p>
       <p>
        Remember to alternate your keys from time to time so that you keep the batteries in both charged.  Some have found success with placing the key into a rechargeable toothbrush charger overnight as well.
       </p>
       <p>
        Official documentation on key initialization can also be viewed at:
        <a class="external free" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/attachment.php?attachmentid=171170&amp;d=1231280426" rel="nofollow">
         http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/attachment.php?attachmentid=171170&amp;d=1231280426
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        Another thing you can do is to replace the battery!  It's not officially possible (or recommended) for the new key design (2000+) but it can be done.  Instructions can be found
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=481585" rel="nofollow">
         in this thread
        </a>
        .  Read the first page or two, but be sure to make note of post #177 about battery terminal positions.  Some have had success soldering in a small extension wire where the terminals didn't line up closely with the circuit board connecting points.  In a pinch, a 3v calculator battery can be used temporarily until your rechargeable arrives.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="DSC.2C_ABS.2C_and_BRAKE_lights_all_illuminated.3F_The_.22trifecta.22_of_lights.2C_wheel_speed_sensors.2C_etc.">
         DSC, ABS, and BRAKE lights all illuminated?  The "trifecta" of lights, wheel speed sensors, etc.
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        This happens when the car has detected a fault and has disabled the DSC and ABS systems.  If you recently drove on ice, a dynamometer, or on another very slippery surface, the car may just /think/ the system has malfunctioned.  Driving a few miles on a regular surface should fix the problem. Sometimes a dying battery will produce odd errors like this as well.
       </p>
       <p>
        Another possible fix is to slowly turn the steering wheel from completely left to completely right, then back again.
       </p>
       <p>
        If you did not recently drive on ice and the wheel turning solution did not work, this is usually caused by either:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         One of your wheel speed / ABS sensors failing (there's one on each wheel) or needs cleaning see
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=554486" rel="nofollow">
          here
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         The DSC pressure sensor on the brake master cylinder is faulty
        </li>
        <li>
         Your steering angle sensor has failed
        </li>
        <li>
         Your battery needs replacement
        </li>
        <li>
         You maybe in need of an alignment
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        An independent BMW mechanic should have the autologic/Modic3/GT1 computer required to read the codes to determine the source of the fault.  If you want to diagnose the problem yourself,
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showpost.php?p=6217953&amp;postcount=6" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        is a post on e46fanatics that describes how to test each wheel speed sensor.   Remove the wheel and identify the wires running from the back of the hub to a disconnectable wiring harness (do not confuse this with the brake pad wear sensor, which is only located on the front left and rear right wheel).    Use the procedure above.  The sensors are about $100 each.
       </p>
       <p>
        The steering angle sensor is accessible from inside the cabin.  You can find a picture of its location by searching for it on www.realoem.com/bmw.
       </p>
       <p>
        An in-depth test of the ABS module and possible loose wire fix is discussed in
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?p=7585674#post7585674" rel="nofollow">
         this thread
        </a>
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="ECU.2FDME_fan_behind_driver.27s_dash">
         ECU/DME fan behind driver's dash
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        See
        <a class="external text" href="http://m3forum.net/m3forum/showthread.php?t=206764" rel="nofollow">
         this link
        </a>
        for discussion of symptoms and replacement.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="I.2FK-Bus_Information">
         I/K-Bus Information
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Technically speaking, both data busses are the same, but used for different modules. I-Bus is mainly used for multimedia devices such as radio, telephone, steering wheel controls, and so on. On other hand, K-Bus is used for modules such as GM or IHKA. However, both busses are connected to instrument cluster (IKE) which acts as a router between two busses. This allows I-Bus module to send a message to module on K-Bus, and vise versa.
       </p>
       <p>
        I/K-Bus (further down referred to as a bus) is using single wire for receiving and sending data; pulled high (12V or VBATT) on idle, and down (GND) to send a bit. It operates at the speed rate of 9600 bits per second, 8 data bits, even parity, and single stop bit.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Message_Structure">
         Message Structure
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Typical message on a bus has a simple structure.
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         <b>
          1byte:
         </b>
         Source ID
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          1byte:
         </b>
         Length
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          1byte:
         </b>
         Destination ID
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          xbyte:
         </b>
         Data
        </li>
        <li>
         <b>
          1byte:
         </b>
         XOR Checksum
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Source_ID.2FDestination_ID">
         Source ID/Destination ID
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        Identification byte of source and destination modules.
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Length">
         Length
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        Length of the message following the length byte. A message with 11 bytes with hava "Length" byte set to 9.
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="XOR_Checksum">
         XOR Checksum
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        Starting with 0x00, each bit in a message is XORed.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Parsing_Messages">
         Parsing Messages
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Because messages on bus have no start or stop indicator, parsing can be quite a challenge. Below are two methods for doing just that.
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Brute-force">
         Brute-force
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        This method is simple and fairly straight forward, but it is not optimal with embedded devices with low resources.
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Interrupt_Timestamp">
         Interrupt Timestamp
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        More complicated, and more optimal for low resource devices or microcontrollers such as arduino.
       </p>
       <p>
        Sources:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         <a class="external free" href="http://web.comhem.se/mulle2/IBUSInsideDRAFTREV5.pdf" rel="nofollow">
          http://web.comhem.se/mulle2/IBUSInsideDRAFTREV5.pdf
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a class="external free" href="http://www.bmwgm5.com/IBUS.htm" rel="nofollow">
          http://www.bmwgm5.com/IBUS.htm
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a class="external free" href="http://sourceforge.net/projects/jibus/" rel="nofollow">
          http://sourceforge.net/projects/jibus/
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a class="external free" href="http://web.comhem.se/bengt-olof.swing/IBus.htm" rel="nofollow">
          http://web.comhem.se/bengt-olof.swing/IBus.htm
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a class="external free" href="http://www.reslers.de/IBUS/" rel="nofollow">
          http://www.reslers.de/IBUS/
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h2>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Engine">
         Engine
        </span>
       </h2>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Alternator_Replacement">
         Alternator Replacement
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        A red battery light on your dash or a car that won't start but has a battery you believe to be good can be signs of a failed or failing alternator.  Check the main electrical connections to confirm they're clean and properly secured.  If the car still has issues but can be driven, most major auto parts stores will test your alternator, battery and starter for free to determine if they're putting out the proper voltage.
       </p>
       <p>
        Replacing an alternator is a fairly easy do-it-yourself.  blog.bavauto.com has an excellent write-up
        <a class="external text" href="http://blog.bavauto.com/bmw-e46/replacing-an-alternato-2001-325i" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        (note: this how-to is for E46s with automatic transmissions; the instructions are identical for a manual transmission except for the radiator fan removal, which is more involved on an automatic).
       </p>
       <p>
        Sometimes, just the voltage regulator can be replaced (black part that bolts onto the back of the unit) for much less than the whole unit.
       </p>
       <p>
        A failed alternator has symptoms nearly identical to a failed battery.  Make certain you have a correct diagnosis before replacing one or the other.
       </p>
       <p>
        After replacing your alternator, do not start the car unless your battery is charged.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Oxygen_Sensor_Replacement">
         Oxygen Sensor Replacement
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Information can be found in these threads:
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=313882" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 1
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=293116" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 2
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        A video for the pre-cat sensors can be found here:
        <a class="external free" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DmW7mo-yLr8" rel="nofollow">
         http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DmW7mo-yLr8
        </a>
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Timing_Chain_Tensioner_Spring_Replacement">
         Timing Chain Tensioner Spring Replacement
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        As the engine gets beyond 150k miles, the timing chain has stretched/worn a little and the tensioner spring has lost some tension so it is probably a good idea to replace the spring.
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=552536" rel="nofollow">
         This thread
        </a>
        has a DIY and some discussion.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="OIL_LEAKS_-_Valve_Cover_Gasket.2C_Crankcase_Vent.2FOil_Separator.2C_Oil_Filter_Housing_Gasket.2C_Oil_Pan_Gasket">
         OIL LEAKS - Valve Cover Gasket, Crankcase Vent/Oil Separator, Oil Filter Housing Gasket, Oil Pan Gasket
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        The most common oil leak spots are the VCG - Valve Cover Gasket (see Engine/Troubleshooting below); CCV - Crankcase Vent/Oil Separator and related hoses(see Maintenance above); the OFHG - Oil Filter Housing Gasket (see Maintenance above); and the Oil Pan Gasket.  Make sure you know exactly where the oil is coming from as all the oil leaks run down and probably make the oil pan gasket look like it's leaking whether it is or not.
       </p>
       <p>
        The oil pan gasket is very difficult to repair as it involves lowering the oil pan, which involves lowering the front subframe cross-brace (metal "belly pan").  See
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=532166&amp;page=7" rel="nofollow">
         this thread
        </a>
        for discussion and DIYs.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="CCV_Explained">
         CCV Explained
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Note: This is an attempt to explain the purpose and work principle of crankcase ventilation valve (CCV/CVV). The information provided is do be consumed with a grain of salt as it is based on online research and observations. Please do edit if mistake is found.
       </p>
       <p>
        Engine produces gasses when it is running. Those gasses are collected in valve cover, and with no where to escape the (positive) pressure will build up and cause the cover to crack (or oil will leak). Dumping those gasses into environment or back into intake would result in one of two problems. First, there would be no pressure in valve cover thus performance will be affected. Second, dumping gasses would pollute air and result in horrible smell near the car. Therefore, crankcase ventilation valve system is the solution.
       </p>
       <p>
        <i>
         Diagram to be added
        </i>
        CCV itself consist of three ports that are used. Bottom port is connected to oil pan; middle port is connected to valve cover; and finally top port is connected to intake vacuum. Topmost part of CCV consists of rubber membrane (orange), spring, and chamber where it is all mounted. The spring, rubber membrane, and intake vacuum work together to regulate the pressure in valve cover to a specific value. More detailed explanation is described below.
       </p>
       <p>
        With engine idling the intake pressure is high, thus membrane closes the intake vacuum port. In this state, all the gasses escape to the oil pan.
When car is being driven or RPMs are increased, increased pressure in valve cover causes the membrane to open intake vacuum port. Until pressure is lowered, some of the gasses are routed to intake manifold.
       </p>
       <p>
        In case of CCV failure, orange membrane is broken causing vacuum leak which will eventually suck up the oil from oil pan.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Troubleshooting_2">
         Troubleshooting
        </span>
       </h3>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Check_Engine.2FService_Engine_Soon_Light_.28CEL.2FSES.29_and_scanning_for_ERROR_CODES">
         Check Engine/Service Engine Soon Light (CEL/SES) and scanning for ERROR CODES
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        The check engine light comes on when the key is turned to position II (key on, engine off) as a test of the bulb/circuit itself.  If your check engine light is on while the car is running, the car's diagnostic computer has detected an error from one of the many monitoring sensors on the car.  Some errors can be as simple as not tightening the gas cap enough (in which case the SES light will turn off by itself after resolving the issue and some driving), or slightly more involved, like a cracked and leaky rubber tube/boot that takes air from the air filter box to the engine (which, to turn off the service light, will require correcting the problem and clearing the code logged in the computer with a scan tool).  The best course of action when this light appears is to obtain a scan tool and scan the computer for the error codes (aka diagnostic trouble codes DTCs).
       </p>
       <p>
        Peake makes scan tools that read BMW specific codes, and there are many "universal" code readers out there from other vendors that will also work very well with your BMW.  Autel makes a popular model, probably due to it's affordability - the MS300.  There are also apps for mobile devices now that can be hooked up to the OBDII port with an adapter - Torque for Android and one for iPhone was released late 2013.  PA Soft for the PC is more expensive but offers in-depth scanning and real-time monitoring of performance parameters.  INPA is also PC based and can be obtained for free on the internet, but is not the easiest to install or use.
       </p>
       <p>
        Solidjake made a short vid explaining how easy it is to use a scan tool
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jvKi-difYss" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        The error codes obtained will help in diagnosing the problem with your car.
       </p>
       <p>
        A list of error codes with descriptions can be found at
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.obd-codes.com/trouble_codes/" rel="nofollow">
         this website
        </a>
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="NO_START">
         NO START
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        BavAuto has a troubleshooting guide published in one of their regular newsletters.
        <b>
         See post #10
        </b>
        in
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=705071" rel="nofollow">
         this thread
        </a>
        Fuel pressure can be checked at the "tire-like" valve on the injector rail with a loaner gauge from autozone, etc.  Pressures in the fuel pressure section below.
       </p>
       <p>
        If you need to
        <b>
         replace your starter
        </b>
        , read this
        <b>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=499230" rel="nofollow">
          entire thread,
         </a>
        </b>
        which starts out with a good DIY and has some good tips towards the end.
       </p>
       <p>
        For help with a faulty ignition switch, see
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/wiki/index.php/BMW_E46#Problems_Starting_with_possible_other_odd_electrical_behavior" rel="nofollow">
         "Problems Starting..."
        </a>
        in the Electrical section above.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Engine_running_rough.2C_stalls_at_idle.2C_etc.3F">
         Engine running rough, stalls at idle, etc?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Misfire_and_Lean_Code_Troubleshooting_P0171_P0174">
         Misfire and Lean Code Troubleshooting P0171 P0174
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        Good thread here:
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=897616" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 1
        </a>
        discussing issues with fuel pumps, DISAs, CCVs, etc.
        <b>
         Includes some DIY guidance
        </b>
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel_Pump_Troubleshooting">
         Fuel Pump Troubleshooting
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        When the key is turned to position 1 (on but not to crank position), you should hear a dull buzz from the passenger back seat area where the pump is.  Checking for voltage at the pump connector - you should read about 5 volts at the pump for about 1 second when the key is turned on.  A fuel filter with greater than 60,000 miles can restrict fuel flow and cause performance issues, and can strain the pump.
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel_Pressure_Specs">
         Fuel Pressure Specs
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        At prime (key on, no start) and while idling:
       </p>
       <p>
        All engines except the S54 3.2L M3 - Fuel pressure 3.5 +/- 0.2 bar or 50.76 +/- 2.9 PSI 
Residual fuel pressure 20 minutes after shutdown  - Fuel pressure &gt;3 bar or &gt;43.51 PSI
       </p>
       <p>
        S54 3.2L M3 - Fuel pressure 5.0 +/- 0.2 bar or 72.5 +/- 2.9 PSI
Residual fuel pressure 20 minutes after shutdown - Fuel pressure &gt;4.5 bar or &gt;62.2 PSI
       </p>
       <p>
        Pressure can be checked at the Schrader valve (looks like regular tire air valve) on the injector rail (under the driver side beauty cover on the engine).  Auto parts stores are reported to loan the pressure gauges.
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel_Volume_Specs">
         Fuel Volume Specs
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        All engines 1.12 liter (1.16 qt) for 30 seconds at 12 Volts or while crank
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Ignition_coils">
         Ignition coils
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        Vehicles with ignition coils from a faulty batch may experience misfiring in one or more cylinders.  The issue is identified via batch numbers of the problem ignition coils, as well as OBD-II diagnostics.
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Camshaft_position_sensors">
         Camshaft position sensors
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        This is usually caused by either bad coils or a bad camshaft position sensor.  Both are common problems, and usually they both 'throw a code' (triggering the service engine soon light).  You can get your 'codes read' for free at any Autozone location to determine the problem.
       </p>
       <p>
        There are two camshaft position sensors, one for the intake and one for the exhaust.  The code should tell you which to replace.  DIYs for the exhaust camshaft position sensor can be found here:
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=332244&amp;highlight=sensor" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 1
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=370814&amp;highlight=sensor" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 2
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=226899&amp;highlight=camshaft+sensor+exhaust" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 3
        </a>
        .
A DIY for the intake camshaft position sensor can be found here:
        <a class="external text" href="http://forums.roadfly.com/forums/bmw/bmw-3-series-e46/forum.php?postid=7616963&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 1
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        TESTING THE CAM SENSOR:  With a multimeter, in
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?p=6582378#post6582378" rel="nofollow">
         this thread.
        </a>
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Crankshaft_position_sensor">
         Crankshaft position sensor
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        See this
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=722808" rel="nofollow">
         thread
        </a>
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Cracked_intake_tube">
         Cracked intake tube
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        Another common problem is the intake tube elbow cracks.  A DIY replacement can be found
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmw330ci.net/maintenance/tubeelbow.php" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="VANOS_failure">
         VANOS failure
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        Idle problems can also be caused by failure of the VANOS system.  You can confirm this by seeing if your idle returns to normal after unplugging the VANOS wiring harness. BMW used an inferior material for the seal support o-rings and it is known to degrade considerably in as little as 40,000 miles, negatively affecting low end torque and engine smoothness in general.
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.beisansystems.com/" rel="nofollow">
         Beisan Systems
        </a>
        (Beisan website has DIY including Valve Cover Gasket replacement)sells improved VANOS Viton seal kits for a DIY rebuild but even better
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.drvanos.com/" rel="nofollow">
         Dr. Vanos
        </a>
        sells completely rebuilt, blue printed and enhanced replacement VANOS units that also have Viton seals installed an are actually better than new BMW units for a very reasonable price.
       </p>
       <p>
        Failed VANOS seals can cause fault codes generated by engine computer.
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=427473/" rel="nofollow">
         In this thread
        </a>
        (post #8) see how VANOS codes P0015 and P0014 were solved by the Beisan kit installation.
       </p>
       <p>
        Also see this
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=510952/" rel="nofollow">
         P0014 code solution thread
        </a>
        where the root cause was the exhaust side vanos actuator (piston behind the solenoid) that was stuck and needed to be reset.  Removal of the solenoid requires a 32mm deep, thin-walled socket, which is not easy to find.  An e39er reported that a 1 11/32
        <i>
         shower valve socket will work and can be found in hardware stores for about $20.
        </i>
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_Air_Control_System_Codes_P0491_.26_P0492">
         Secondary Air Control System Codes P0491 &amp; P0492
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        The secondary air system pumps fresh air through holes in the exhaust valves to help the catalytic converters deal with the extra fuel in the exhaust vapor for the first minute or so on a cold start (when the engine runs rich, prior to settling to stable idle).
       </p>
       <p>
        For troubleshooting and repair help of codes P0491 and P0492 see
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=430048&amp;highlight=p0491/" rel="nofollow">
         this thread
        </a>
        by Starless
       </p>
       <p>
        It has also been reported that the passages in the exhaust valves can clog and restrict the flow of air and some have had success with a seafoam procedure.  WARNING: This will produce and unbelievable amount of smoke from the exhaust so be forewarned.  See
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=711460&amp;highlight=secondary" rel="nofollow">
         this link
        </a>
       </p>
       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Vacuum_Fittings_on_Rear_and_Underside_of_Intake_Manifold">
         Vacuum Fittings on Rear and Underside of Intake Manifold
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        See
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=724498" rel="nofollow">
         this thread
        </a>
        for a good picture of the rear (post #2).
       </p>
       <p>
        See
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=678522" rel="nofollow">
         this thread
        </a>
        for pics of the underside (post #17).
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_Airflow.28MAF.29Sensor_Testing">
         Mass Airflow(MAF)Sensor Testing
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        If you get a code indicating a bad MAF sensor, you can try to diagnose by reading fuel trims with an appropriate scan tool and apply these tests with a multimeter, as discussed in
        <b>
         <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=1018366&amp;highlight=maf+pin+test" rel="nofollow">
          this thread.
         </a>
        </b>
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Horrible_Burning_Smell.2FSmoke_coming_from_rear.2Fpassenger.28US.29_side_of_engine_.28Valve_Cover_Gasket-VCG.29">
         Horrible Burning Smell/Smoke coming from rear/passenger(US) side of engine (Valve Cover Gasket-VCG)
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Most likely your valve cover gasket (VCG) has failed and needs replacement.  Can usually confirm by inspecting the silver heat shield over the exhaust manifold and blotting a clean paper towel along the passenger side of the engine where the valve cover meets the head, looking for fresh oil.  See VANOS failure above for procedures on the VCG replacement.  It's a good time to refresh the seals in the VANOS at this time as the valve cover has to come off for VANOS service.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_light_.28yellow_or_red.29_illuminates_during_driving_or_after_shutting_the_car_off.3F">
         Oil light (yellow or red) illuminates during driving or after shutting the car off?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        First, make sure you have enough oil.  If you do, then your oil level sensor is defective.  Please see this thread for DIY replacement information:
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=366659&amp;highlight=Yellow+Oil+Light" rel="nofollow">
         TheYellowOilLightLink
        </a>
        .  If you don't have enough oil check your engine block for leaks.  There are several known common gasket failures that could lead to an oil leak.  The valve cover gasket is a common issue as is the oil housing gasket.  The spark plug replacement section under other maintenance has a DIY on replacing the valve cover gasket.  You can also follow the Beisan DIY
        <a class="external autonumber" href="http://beisansystems.com/procedures/vanos_procedure.htm" rel="nofollow">
         [15]
        </a>
        on doing a VANOS replacement as it is the same procedure, just ignore the VANOS section.  The oil housing gasket section other maintenance has a DIY on replacing the oil housing gasket.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="My_car_whines_when_I_turn_the_steering_wheel">
         My car whines when I turn the steering wheel
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        You may need a new power steering pump.  A great replacement DIY can be found
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=575499&amp;highlight=power+steering" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Electrical_Connector_Junction_Box.2F.22Where_does_this_connector_go.3F.22">
         Electrical Connector Junction Box/"Where does this connector go?"
        </span>

       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Sock_Mod_-_Solve_that_power_steering_fluid_splash_problem">
         Sock Mod - Solve that power steering fluid splash problem
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Power steering fluid splashing around your engine compartment?
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_1pzRJMwRx0" rel="nofollow">
         Watch this DIY

        for a track proven solution. jvr826 explains the aftermarket solutions available and brings you thru the step-by-step installation process.

       <h2>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel_System">
         Fuel System
        </span>
       </h2>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="What_fuel_grade_should_I_use.3F">
         What fuel grade should I use?
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Your owners manual states you should use premium (At least 91 octane as measured by the R+M/2 method in the US).  If you use a lesser grade fuel, your car will retard timing to avoid detonation, which will decrease fuel economy and reduce power.  Premium fuel is even less of a price premium as gas prices increase since it's almost always either 20 or 25 cents higher than regular.  Using regular might cost you more because you'll get less gas mileage but you will hear pinging (mostly in the summer) when mileage drops.
       </p>
       <p>
        It is also recommended to add one bottle of Chevron Techron or BMW Fuel Injector cleaner every 3,000-5,000 miles or once per oil change.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel_Pump_Problems">
         Fuel Pump Problems
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        See
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/wiki/index.php/BMW_E46#Misfire_and_Lean_Code_Troubleshooting" rel="nofollow">
         Misfire and Lean Code (P0171 and P0174) Troubleshooting
        </a>
        above in Engine section
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Leak_Detection_Pump_.28LDP.29.2FCharcoal_Canister_DIY">
         Leak Detection Pump (LDP)/Charcoal Canister DIY
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Usually you get codes specific to problems here.  Check out
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=538442" rel="nofollow">
         this thread
        </a>
        Also and the end of that thread there is a link with a tip for helping to get EVAP and CCM to set when they are stubborn.
       </p>
       <h2>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Interior">
         Interior
        </span>
       </h2>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="What_is_the_sensor.2Flight_by_my_headlight_switch.3F">
         What is the sensor/light by my headlight switch?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        It is a light sensor which affects how brightly the on board computer and radio lights are displayed, based on how bright it is in the cabin. Test it out by getting in your car at night, starting it, turning on the headlights, then taking the flashlight out of the glove compartment and shining it at the sensor. The displays mentioned above should become much brighter.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="What_is_the_red_knob_below_the_rear-view_mirror.3F">
         What is the red knob below the rear-view mirror?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        This is commonly referred to as the "clown nose". It houses a LED that flashes when the alarm is armed. For cars without the premium package (which includes the auto-dimming rear view), it also functions as the dimming lever- Just twist it!
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="How_do_I_know_if_I.27ve_got_leather_or_leatherette.3F">
         How do I know if I've got leather or leatherette?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Please see
        <b>
         post 95 of
         <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?p=15837800#post15837800" rel="nofollow">
          this thread
         </a>
        </b>
        over on E46Fanatics.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Interior_trim_removal.2Freplacement">

       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="My_window_doesn.27t_go_all_the_way_up.2Fdown_or_makes_bad_noises_.28WINDOW_REGULATOR.29">
         My window doesn't go all the way up/down or makes bad noises (WINDOW REGULATOR)
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        This is almost always the window regulator, a known failure point.
Here are some do-it-yourself replacement instructions:
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=104035" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 1
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=104035&amp;highlight=door+trim" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 2
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=356847" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 3 (BEST "zip-tie")
        </a>
        .
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showpost.php?p=2470622&amp;postcount=4" rel="nofollow">
         Here
        </a>
        and
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showpost.php?p=4702144&amp;postcount=4" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        are other posts with good tips. Additional observations
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=421824" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
        <b>
         Removing the door panel on coupes
        </b>
        - there are three screws in the door handle, one behind the circle cover in the open/pull lever cavity, and one behind the little airbag badge.  Then start pulling at the lower panel corner just like on the sedans.  Inside the door, the window is held to the lift bracket with an external torx bolt (E7?), vs. a low-profile hex head bolt on the sedans.
       </p>
       <p>
        It's believed that the windows sticking to the rubber seals when closed stresses the plastic cable-holder on opening, and this can be lessened by treating your seals so they don't stick - "gummiflege" or glycerine.  Also, lubing the lifting tracks on the regulator can help - some say white lithium grease but the original grease is a thicker, sticky grease (probably waterproof since that part of the door sees water), which may be sold as a "waterproof grease" at auto parts stores.  Some recommend a squirt of a silicone-type of oil at the top of the window channels near the top of the door.  Less binding, less stress on the plastic cable-holder or zip-tie fix.  Careful with the foam vapor barrier, cut the tarry adhesive with a thin flexible knife and heat with hairdryer to make more pliable/ensure good reseal.  You can buy more of the adhesive "ribbon seal" at auto parts stores if you need to refresh.  Also don't lose the felt grommets off all the plastic pop rivets for the door panel.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="My_window_auto-up.2Fdown_does_not_work">
         My window auto-up/down does not work
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        You can reset the window auto function by:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Turn the key to the ON position but do not start the car
        </li>
        <li>
         Roll the windows all the way down, THEN roll them all the way up and HOLD the switch up for an additional 5-10 seconds.
        </li>
        <li>
         Turn the key off.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Sunroof_problems">
         Sunroof problems
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Sunroof won't auto-close (it reverses in auto mode) and clips broken?  Repair info can be found
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=222850" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
Cartridge/Track broken?  DIY replacement information can be found here:
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=285479&amp;highlight=sunroof+clip" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 1
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        To reset sunroof if won't close, hold button in up position (towards roof) for 20 seconds, then push forward.  This may resolve problem.
       </p>
       <p>
        When screwing the glass back on to the slide mounts be sure to push the glass up slightly so that the screws do not rest on the slide mount, it will not allow enough clearance for the roof to open and close properly. You will most likely also notice a large gap due to the sunroof sitting up to a 1/4" lower then the top of the roof.
       </p>
       <h2>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Navigation">
         Navigation
        </span>
       </h2>
       <dl>
        <dd>
         <i>
          Main article:
          <a href="/wiki/index.php/Navigation" title="Navigation">
           Navigation
          </a>
         </i>
        </dd>
       </dl>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Versions_of_the_NAV_in_the_E46">
         Versions of the NAV in the E46
        </span>
       </h3>
       <ul>
        <li>
         The MK2 NAV system (CD based) was available from start of production to 05/2000 production date E46s
        </li>
        <li>
         The MK3 NAV system (CD based) was available from 06/2000 to 09/2002 production date E46s.  In 2002, it received a 16x9 widescreen display (with a cassette behind it)
        </li>
        <li>
         The MKIV NAV system (DVD based) was available from 10/2002 production on.  It is a 16x9 widescreen display with either a cassette, minidisk or CD player behind it)
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h2>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Exterior_.2F_Body">
         Exterior / Body
        </span>
       </h2>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Wheels.2FTires">
         Wheels/Tires
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        There are many wheels available for the E46.  The bolt pattern is 5x120, 72mm center bore, and the offset for both front and rear need to be between +35 and +50, and fitting the outer limits of that range will depend on selected tire size.   323/325/328s can use 16" or bigger wheels.   The 330s must use 17" or bigger wheels to clear the brakes, with two exceptions - there are two known 16" wheels that will fit over the 330s brakes: the ASA JH3, and the 16x7.5 AT Italia Type 5.
       </p>
       <p>
        Most E46s with the sport package came with staggered wheels and tires; that is, the rears are wider than the fronts.  This /negatively/ affects performance because it encourages understeer. Of course, understeer is safer than oversteer, so that's the way BMW err's.
       </p>
       <p>
        The widest non-staggered size that you can run seems to be 255/35/18.  jvr826 has these on 18x8.5 wheels with a +42 offset and KrisL has these on 4 rear ZHP wheels (18x8.5 with a +50 offset).
       </p>
       <p>
        Rear M3 wheels will NOT fit on a non-M3 (the rear M3 offset is +24), but the fronts will.  You can buy four FRONT M3 wheels and put them on all four corners of a non-M car.  If you're wondering "what it would take to get rear M3 wheels on the car"... it would take thousands of dollars in body work to get the fenders wide enough - its just not worth it when there are many great aftermarket wheel designs that will look and fit great, as well as giving you a nice staggered look, if that's what you're after.  Check out the offerings by umnitza.com, jlevisw.com, europeanautosource.com, etc.
       </p>
       <p>
        5-series wheels have a different center bore/hub size and therefore should not be used. For standard BMW bore/hub size reference please see
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmwforums.info/bmw-wheels-forum/333-bmw-wheel-hub-diameter-sizes-hub-centre-bore-sizes-et-offset.html" rel="nofollow">
         this information
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        When removing alloy wheels, note that a galvanic reaction may have set in between the alloy and the wheel hub, "sticking" the wheel to the hub.  To encourage the wheel to come off, jack the car up with your preferred method, so the tire is approximately 1" off the ground.  Using a heavy (e.g. sledge) hammer, place a block of thick wood (e.g. 4 X 4) behind the wheel.  Hit until the wheel is dislodged.  You may have to alternate sides of the wheel.
       </p>
       <p>
        Before replacing the wheel, smear a thin layer of quality lithium grease on the wheel hub landing.  This will make removal of the wheel easier next time.
       </p>
       <p>
        For more information or other questions, please post them in the
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/forumdisplay.php?f=49" rel="nofollow">
         TireRack sponsored Tire forum here at Bimmerfest
        </a>
        .
       </p>

       <h5>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Jet_Fockin.27_Black">
         Jet Fockin' Black
        </span>
       </h5>
       <p>
        Warining: Don't make your tires JFB!
        <a class="external text" href="http://my.is/forums/f87/crashed-my-baby-147582/" rel="nofollow">
         Link
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Aerodynamics.2FBody_Kits">
         Aerodynamics/Body Kits
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        The aerodynamics packages installed on E46 cars from the factory varied according to model year, body style and trim level. Flexible ordering/optioning ensured that customers in European and most world markets typically had a variety of aerodynamics packages to choose from.
       </p>
       <p>
        In the US market, a more specific set of guidelines can be used to determine the aerodynamics package installed on a particular car:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Prefacelift sedan (1999-2001 323i/325i/328i/330i)
        </li>
        <li>
         Prefacelift coupe/convertible (2000-2003 323Ci/325Ci/328Ci/330Ci)
        </li>
        <li>
         Prefacelift BMW Accessories Aero Kit (optional dealer installed accessory kit for prefacelift cars; very rare)
        </li>
        <li>
         Facelift sedan (2002-2005 325i/330i)
        </li>
        <li>
         Facelift coupe/convertible (2004-2006 325Ci/330Ci)
        </li>
        <li>
         M-tech I (2001-2005 330i with ZSP/Sport package, sedan only including prefacelift)
        </li>
        <li>
         M-tech II (2003-2005 330i with ZHP/Performance package / 2004-2006 330Ci with ZHP)
        </li>
        <li>
         M3 (2001-2006 M3, all)
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        In most world markets, the M-tech aerodynamic kits were associated with M-sport equipped cars. The original M-tech I design was superseded by M-tech II during later production years. In the US market, M-tech I was found on ZSP equipped 330 sedans regardless of production year and M-tech II was only available with the ZHP options package.
       </p>
       <p>
        Many aftermarket body kits of varying qualities are available for the E46. The most popular OEM retrofit kit is M-tech II (standard equipment on ZHP).  You can purchase it from your local dealer or online from somewhere like www.bavauto.com for $900-1000.  They come unpainted, so you will have to get it painted by a body shop.
       </p>
       <p>
        Other body kits may be bought from Bimmerfest sponsors. This includes a wide range or front and rear bumpers, side skirts, vented hoods and other aftermarket parts. Fitments of these parts are made for almost all models, sedan, coupe and convertible.
       </p>
       <h4>

       <p>

       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Lighting">
         Lighting
        </span>
       </h3>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Halogen_Headlight_Bulb_Replacement_Tip">
         Halogen Headlight Bulb Replacement Tip
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Make sure you put the bulb into the socket oriented the same way as the one you're replacing.  If it's off 180 degrees, you may not be able to remount the socket into the lens housing.  If you have difficulty remounting with the new bulb, try taking the bulb out of the socket and rotating 180 degrees, then remount the socket to the lens housing.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Clear_turn_signals">
         Clear turn signals
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Your best bet is to stick with OEM if you want 'clear corners'.  Aftermarket lenses are of varying quality and may leak.  The OEM clear corners are manufactured by ULF and can be purchased by many companies such as www.bekkers.com, www.bavauto.com, etc.
       </p>
       <p>
        DEPO lenses used to be poor quality, but recent reports are promising and have shown that the quality has improved. They can be purchased much cheaper than OEM from places like www.jlevisw.com.
       </p>
       <p>
        Installation is very easy... thanks to my330i.com for these DIYs:
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.my330i.com/mod31.php" rel="nofollow">
         Front/side install DIY for 2002+ Sedan
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.my330i.com/mod32.php" rel="nofollow">
         Rear install DIY for 2002+ Sedan
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.my330i.com/mod2.php" rel="nofollow">
         Front/side install DIY for 1999-2001 Sedan
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.my330i.com/mod7.php" rel="nofollow">
         Rear install DIY for 1999-2001 Sedan
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        Another DIY guide can be found on the forums:
        <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=404184" rel="nofollow">
         [18]
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        Facelift coupes use a #7440 type bulb for the front turn signals, not a #7507 as indicated on Sylvania's Lamp Guide.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Angel.2FDemon_Eyes">
         Angel/Demon Eyes
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        <a href="/wiki/index.php/Angel_Eyes" title="Angel Eyes">
         Angel Eyes
        </a>
        or Demon Eyes are lighted rings around the headlights.  They are standard on E39 (and newer) 5-series cars as well as E90 (new 3-series cars).
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.umnitza.com" rel="nofollow">
         Umnitza (www.umnitza.com)
        </a>
        makes a kit (Predator Chromium) that can be retrofitted into existing headlights.  For prefacelift cars, the headlights simply snap open.  Facelift headlights must be baked in an oven to be opened up.
       </p>
       <p>
        There is a new brighter kit out called Predator Orion V2 - available exclusively at Umnitza.com
More information can be found here:
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.m3forum.net/m3forum/showthread.php?t=204548" rel="nofollow">
         POV2
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        Solidjake made a few videos of the V2's in action. They can be found
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RjecAYNDji4" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        and
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=yh48V-uw1Gc" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        Another forum sponsor,
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.europeanautosource.com" rel="nofollow">
         European Auto Source
        </a>
        , now sells a very similar product for less money - the MYCARR angel eyes.  A comparison between these and the Predator Chromium kit can be found here:
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=551664&amp;highlight=mycarr+angel+eyes" rel="nofollow">
         My Carr Angel Eyes
        </a>
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Xenon_retrofit">
         Xenon retrofit
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Your best bet for installing projector Xenon lights in a car that does not have them available is a plug-and-play headlight replacement such as the Umnitza ( www.umnitza.com ) Projector46 with Orion V2 kit.  They can even be purchased with angel eyes pre-installed. They offer a solution that does not require any reflashing.
       </p>
       <p>
        Complete used OEM HID assemblies are also available via Ebay, forum "for-sale" sections, and other sources. Typical prices for a complete set of used (but intact and working) HID headlights range from $400 to $600. Purchasing brand new assemblies via the dealership or an importer is not recommended as the price is generally exorbitant (e.g. $1,100 -- per side).   You not only need the lights, but you also need a new LCM (light control module) and it coded to your car.  This can add another few hundred dollars.
       </p>
       <p>
        You may disable the "headlight out" warning by pulling fuse #32. Note that this will not disable the actual light out warning (which would occur if the lights were switched to the on position and one or both failed to activate), only the passive warning which is only triggered when the headlights are set to be off.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="LED_Tail_Light_Retrofitting_and_Troubleshooting">
         LED Tail Light Retrofitting and Troubleshooting
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Please see these threads over on E46Fanatics:
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=168190&amp;highlight=taillight" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 1
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?s=&amp;threadid=88439" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 2
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=286464&amp;highlight=led+diy" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 3
        </a>
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=161717&amp;highlight=taillight" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 4
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        If your blinker stops working or dims considerably, many have had success restoring function with some light soldering on one of the resistor packs.  See
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=868595" rel="nofollow">
         this thread
        </a>
        over on E46Fanatics.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Lighting_troubleshooting">
         Lighting troubleshooting
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        E46 High Intensity Discharge (HID) Xenon lights use D2S bulbs.  The bulbs come stock in 4300K color temperature, however aftermarket bulbs are available in higher color temperature colors from aftermarket suppliers.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Are_your_Bi-Xenon_headlights_dimmer_than_you_last_remember.3F">
         Are your Bi-Xenon headlights dimmer than you last remember?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        In some cases, the inside of the headlamp projector bowl may be burnt and/or discolored.
       </p>
       <p>
        One option is to replace the headlamp projector bowls.  Checkout eBay or similar as the ZKW projector bowls are not available as replacement parts, and the entire assembly lists for approximately $1,200 -- for each side.
       </p>
       <p>
        If you find a bowl, a DIY to replace the headlamp projector bowls for ZKW Bi-Xenon headlights is shown in
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=332078&amp;highlight=" rel="nofollow">
         this thread
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        Another option is the Lightwerkz TFX projector upgrade. This involves removing your headlamp assemblies and sending them to Lightwerkz in New Jersey to have Infiniti and Acura hardware retrofitted into your headlamp assemblies. Note that this does not affect the HID bulb or the auto-leveling motor. More information is available at
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=418999&amp;highlight=lightwerkz+tfx" rel="nofollow">
         = this thread
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Are_your_Xenon_auto-leveling_headlights_pointing_down.3F">
         Are your Xenon auto-leveling headlights pointing down?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        The plastic arm for the front self-leveling sensor is likely broken.  It's visible with a flashlight by turning your wheels all the way to the right and looking above the right control arm.  It's possible to epoxy it back in place (I actually wrapped a zip tie around the whole arm, then used epoxy liberally around the whole thing).  The part is what bolt #4 touches to in
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.realoem.com/bmw/showparts.do?model=EV53&amp;mospid=47725&amp;btnr=31_0409&amp;hg=31&amp;fg=05&amp;hl=1" rel="nofollow">
         this picture
        </a>
        .
If your late-model self-leveling headlamps are made by ALS/Bosch, the inner pivot next to the levelling solenoid mechanism in the headlamp is prone to breakage. With care and patience you may be able to wire up the broken part as a workaround.
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=379708" rel="nofollow">
         This thread
        </a>
        may help to understand the issue.
       </p>
       <p>
        It is also possible for the link from the front lower control arm to the leveling sensor to become inverted if the suspension is relaxed, such as when changing a tire.  When the suspension is reloaded the arm folds down and tells the sensor the front of the car is pointing up.  This may not be readily apparent during a visual inspection.  The link should be vertical, rather than horizontal.  See this thread for more information:
        <a class="external free" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=781369" rel="nofollow">
         http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=781369
        </a>
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_Add-ons">
         Other Add-ons
        </span>
       </h3>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Euro OEM split mirror.  The outer third of the mirror is convex, eliminating your blind spots.  For the coupe &amp; convertible, the part number is "51 16 8 247 131" (left) and "51 16 8 247 132" (right).  For the sedan, the mirror is square, so it's the same part number for both the left and right (51 16 8 250 438).  Generally, you only want to order a left side mirror on a left drive car since the right mirror is already convex.  Please see the "parts" section of this Wiki for where to order BMW parts.  More info can be found
         <a class="external text" href="http://bimmer.roadfly.com/bmw/forums/e46/forum.php?postid=136385&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow">
          here
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         Black grille.  www.bimmian.com (among other sites) sells black kidney grilles.  On performance package cars (which have gloss black window trim), the kidney grille is the only chrome on the car; therefore, it's a common mod to replace it with a jet black grille.
        </li>
        <li>
         Front "blank" bumper strip (sedan/wagon only).  BMW part # 51-11-8-195-304 replaces the standard front license plate bracket, eliminating it.
        </li>
        <li>
         BMW (Westfalia) hidden tow-bar/towing hitch
        </li>
        <li>
         M3 CSL carbon fibre trunk lid
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Troubleshooting_4">
         Troubleshooting
        </span>
       </h3>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Door_Lock_Cylinder_Broken.3F">
         Door Lock Cylinder Broken?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Once you get your door open, the cylinder can be replaced or rebuilt fairly easily.  It's held in by one allen-head screw.  See this
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=443970&amp;highlight=lock+cylinder" rel="nofollow">
         thread
        </a>
        for rebuild info.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Getting_an_odd_rattle_from_the_rear.3F">
         Getting an odd rattle from the rear?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        If your car was made before October 2002 production, the rear springs have a tendency to break.  You can remove a wheel to see it.  There's a TSB on it
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=496579" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Yet_more_knocks_from_the_trunk.3F">
         Yet more knocks from the trunk?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        The sound deadening material on the spare tire compartment may be damaged or missing, causing the wheel of the spare tire to rattle against the metal, which can be solved with a sheet of rubber.
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=385841" rel="nofollow">
         Here is a quick DIY thread by Jcourcoul
        </a>
        on how to do that.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Strut_towers_.27mushrooming.27">
         Strut towers 'mushrooming'
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Depending on road conditions and how hard a vehicle is driven, the bolts fastening the front shocks to the strut towers are prone to bending outwards over time due to a lack of re-inforcement at the top of the shock towers.  This can affect your alignment and handling.  There are two cures for this problem: Install the stronger strut tower spacers from the 4x4 (See DIY
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmw330ci.net/projects/struttower.php" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        ), or install a (M3)
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.realoem.com/bmw/showparts.do?model=BD52&amp;mospid=47620&amp;btnr=51_5992&amp;hg=51&amp;fg=95&amp;hl=1" rel="nofollow">
         strut brace
        </a>
        between the two shock towers, as
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=32448" rel="nofollow">
         shown here
        </a>
        .
       </p>

       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Straight_line_performance_.2F_Horsepower">
         Straight line performance / Horsepower
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        The E46, like most BMWs, gain very little from typical performance modifications.  If you were to buy a cold air intake, software, headers, exhaust, and underdrive pullies, you'd be lucky to gain 20-25hp and you'd be $1500-3000 poorer.  Forced induction (supercharger or turbocharger) is the only solution for real power gains.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Forced_Induction_-_Turbo_and_Supercharging">
         Forced Induction - Turbo and Supercharging
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Kits are available from companies like VF Engineering, Active Autoworke, Technique Tuning, Dinan, and ESS.  They typically run $5000-7000 + installation and can usually give you about a 50% hp/torque boost over stock.  Some recent discussion
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=730468&amp;highlight=" rel="nofollow">
         here, with good info starting at
         <b>
          post #9
         </b>
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="How_to_avoid_a_CEL_when_installing_aftermarket_headers">
         How to avoid a CEL when installing aftermarket headers
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=486937" rel="nofollow">
         Here
        </a>
        is a thread describing solutions.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Differentials">
         Differentials
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        A shorter differential is the only significant performance booster without forced induction.   A differential swap is best performed by a shop ( preferably performance-oriented).  Switching to a shorter (higher-numerically) ratio allows the engine to get into the fat part of it`s power band more quickly because it`s spinning a bit faster in any given gear  (kind of like your old 10-speed bike which would accelerate much faster on the small front sprocket as opposed to the big one). For example, changing from a 3.07 gear to a 3.46 gear would give the car lots of extra grunt out of second-gear corners, and would reduce the need for downshifts when passing, etc. The downsides are higher engine RPMs(noise) at highway speeds, and slightly reduced gas mileage.... but with a MUCH higher "fun factor".
       </p>
       <p>
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=145570" rel="nofollow">
         Here
        </a>
        is a great thread walking you through swapping your own differential.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="How_can_I_find_out_what_differentials_are_compatible.3F">
         How can I find out what differentials are compatible?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Follow
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bokchoys.com/differential/diy_diff.htm" rel="nofollow">
         this link
        </a>
        for more information.
       </p>
       <p>
        The input flanges from the (323-325) differentials are different than those in the (328-330).  You may have to swap input flanges depending on where you are getting your diff.
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=359219&amp;highlight=diff+flange" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        is a great DIY on swapping the flanges.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Turning_ability">
         Turning ability
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        While BMWs are known to be great handling cars, there are certainly plenty of suspension upgrades available:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Powerflex control arm bushings (www.bimmerworld.com) will make turn-in a bit crisper
        </li>
        <li>
         Rear trailing arm bushing limiters (www.motor-force.com) will reduce excessive toe change under cornering force
        </li>
        <li>
         Sway bars (many options such as UUC's SwayBarbarians, www.uucmotorwerks.com) are often referred to as the best suspension mod bang for the buck.  They actually make your suspension LESS independent, but greatly reduce body roll with very little tradeoffs.
        </li>
        <li>
         Shocks/Struts and springs are available.   If you have a car without the sport or performance packages, simply swapping sport/performance package suspension bits will help quite a bit.  If you want to go further, consider adjustable shocks, lowering springs or full coilover kits from GroundControl, Tein, or TC Kline.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="UUC_Swaybarbarian_install">
