       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Removing_Weight">
         Removing Weight
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Removing weight from an E46 improves all performance aspects as well as mileage, but often at the expense of luxury and comfort items.
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showpost.php?p=6652802&amp;postcount=161" rel="nofollow">
         Here
        </a>
        is a great thread about what you can remove.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Driver_Skill">
         Driver Skill
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        This is where the biggest "bang for the buck" modification is - and you can 'transfer' this mod to any vehicle you drive!   The BMW Car Club of America's local chapters hold autocrosses, car control clinics, and high performance driving schools.   You think you're a good driver - until you go against some of the BMWCCA's instructors.  It's truly a humbling experience that shows you how much skill is truly involved in going fast.
       </p>
       <h2>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Steering_.26_Suspension">
         Steering &amp; Suspension
        </span>
       </h2>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Shocks_and_struts">
         Shocks and struts
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        badenscarpages.ca has a write-up for replacing shocks and struts
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.badenscarpages.ca/e46-shock-strut-replacement/" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Springs">
         Springs
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Springs can break, especially in the rear and may not be easily detected.  A clang sound or creaking when cornering or going over bumps can be an indication.  See
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=124357" rel="nofollow">
         this thread
        </a>
        for discussion, with a good DIY video linked in
        <b>
         post #39.
        </b>
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="What_was_the_steering_retrofit.3F">
         What was the steering retrofit?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        BMW marketing had feedback that said that their cars took too much effort to turn the wheel in slow speed situations, i.e. parking. BMW modified the steering rack and system to decrease the steering effort. Those owners who have had extensive experience with E36's (previous generation 3 series) or pre June 2000 cars have stated that there was also a resulting loss of road feel through the steering wheel. Many of these board members have dubbed the "new" steering feel equipped cars as the "Ultimate Parking Machine".
       </p>
       <p>
        Various owners have stated that the only E46's spared this steering boost and loss in road feel are those equipped with the all wheel drive option (i.e. Xi's).
       </p>
       <p>
        Current rumors state that the steering rack was modified again starting in Jan. 1, 2001 and that the "old" steering was phased in. Some E46s produced between Jan and April may or may not have the "old" steering. If you are unsure, check out post April 2001 cars and compare steering feel. See these posts from "Ginger" and Jon S.
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmer.org/3series/messages/archive/msgsy2001w08/41754.html" rel="nofollow">
         Post 1
        </a>
        &amp;
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmer.org/3series/messages/archive/msgsy2001w10/55279.html" rel="nofollow">
         Post 2
        </a>
        . Those with post-April 1, 2001 have stated that the steering feel was indeed not pre-June 2000 feel, but somewhere in between the "new" (June-Dec 2000) and the old (pre-June 2000). The post April 2001 steering has been dubbed as the "new-new" steering. This change was a direct result of feedback through bimmer.org members posting on the E46 board and direct contact with BMW NA. So our voice does count!
       </p>
       <p>
        So the current terminology is:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         "old" feel: pre-June 2000 build
        </li>
        <li>
         "new" feel: June through December 2000 and some Jan-April 2001
        </li>
        <li>
         "new-new" feel: post April 2001
        </li>
        <li>
         "retrofit" feel: early retrofit "pilot" run participants have stated that the retrofit feels somewhere between the "new-new" and the "old" feel.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        In response to consumer feedback, BMW NA initiated a program to satisfy owners of MY2001 E46s who prefer less boost in the power steering system. These owners maintain that a loss of 'feel' was associated with the newer systems which had more boost than MY2000 and earlier E46s. Intitially, BMW NA maintained a list of owners who would be interested in changing their steering racks for systems with less boost. People who have called in to have their name added to a list of persons interested in a retrofit back in Jan/Feb began to be contacted starting the week of April 16, 2001 en masse. BMW NA is going through the list and contacting those with 323/325 and 330's that were produced between June and December 2000, and is offering a one-time free-of-charge changeover to a less boosted steering system.
       </p>
       <p>
        BMWNA has been very clear on the statements to those contacted. They typically cover the following items:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Steering rack and components will be replaced with pre-June 2000 components at no charge.
        </li>
        <li>
         You have your choice of BMW centers to install the retrofit.
        </li>
        <li>
         BMWNA will contact your chose center to give them the details and parts needed for the retrofit. BMWNA requests a couple of days before you try to schedule an appointment with your center.
        </li>
        <li>
         BMWNA makes it very clear that the retrofit will make steering more difficult at lower speeds.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        There has been some confusion as to whether June-Dec 2000 325's and post Jan 2001 cars with "new-new" feel were eligible for the retrofit. Latest news is that the post Jan 325/330's are eligible due to the phase in started in Jan 2001. "New-new" feel cars might be and will be evaluated on a case by case basis according to some sources.
       </p>

       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Troubleshooting_5">
         Troubleshooting
        </span>
       </h3>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Car_doesn.27t_feel_as_crisp_as_it_once_did.3F">
         Car doesn't feel as crisp as it once did?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Control arms and control arm bushings are common failure points in the E46.  Control arm bushings can last as little as 40-60k miles with the control arms themselves not far behind.  The most common symptom is the steering not feeling as crisp as it once did; however, there are other worse symptoms such as the car wanting to turn when you jab the brakes.
       </p>
       <p>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.oembimmerparts.com" rel="nofollow">
         OEM Bimmer Parts
        </a>
        is a Bimmerfest sponsor that sells control arms and control arm bushings.
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerworld.com" rel="nofollow">
         BimmerWorld
        </a>
        is a retailer that sells aftermarket arms and powerflex (stiffer) bushings. For the AWD XI models, the control arms, bushings, etc are different than the standard RWD models, and require a slightly different replacement procedure.
       </p>
       <p>
        Here are control arm replacement DIYs:
       </p>
       <ul>
        <li>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.e46fanatics.com/forum/showthread.php?t=364978" rel="nofollow">
          Thread 1
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.e46fanatics.com/features/feature.php?news_id=67" rel="nofollow">
          Thread 2
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=335402&amp;page=2&amp;highlight=control+arms" rel="nofollow">
          Thread 3
         </a>
         .
        </li>
        <li>
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LXoBRKQeT44" rel="nofollow">
          A great YouTube Video showing how to replace them
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=778979" rel="nofollow">
          XI Specific
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h4>

       <h3>

        </span>

       </p>

       <p>
        If you're budget minded, understeer.com has an line of modified BMW levers to suit your car.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Clutch_Delay_Valve">
         Clutch Delay Valve
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        The clutch delay valve is a small valve in the clutch line that restricts clutch fluid flow.  It's designed to prevent shock to the transmission if the clutch is dropped.  The bad part is that it makes the clutch feel vague and can make it difficult to pull off smooth shifts for experienced manual transmission drivers.
       </p>
       <p>
        Note that installation of a restricted CDV was not made on all manual cars. There are some that do not have one, some that do have one without restriction (same as the delete version) and then a lot of cars that have a restricted CDV. Seems that earlier E46 do not have it and it was phased in sometime in 2001 built dates.
       </p>
       <p>
        There are two choices:  Remove the CDV completely (the two ends of the clutch line will screw into each other, requiring no parts) or replace the CDV with a drilled-out version, eliminating the restriction.  People use the drilled-out version to avoid dealer hassles in case a transmission warranty issue arises.
       </p>
       <p>
        After replacing or removing the CDV, you do need to bleed the clutch line.
       </p>
       <p>
        More information, as well as where to purchase a drilled-out CDV, can be found
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.zeckhausen.com/CDV.htm" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        Paul180's CDV replacement DIY can be found
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmw330ci.net/projects/cdv.php" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Clutch_stop">
         Clutch stop
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Another cause of poor clutch feel is that the factory clutch stop (the plastic piece that prevents the clutch from depressing any further) is too low; that is, you don't need it to go down as far as it does.  You can purchase clutch stops from many aftermarket companies (UUC, Rogue), but I made my own.  More information can be found
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=160300" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Transmission_mounts">
         Transmission mounts
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        A DIY for installing UUC Transmission mounts can be found
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bmw330ci.net/projects/transmounts.php" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Auto_----.3E_5_speed_conversion">
         Auto ----&gt; 5 speed conversion
        </span>
       </h3>
       <p>
        Neil1138, a regular on E46Fanatics, released a great DIY on how to perform a complete manual transmission conversion on your E46! Included inside are detailed mechanical procedures and even a complete coding section required to finish the transformation! Link

         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Troubleshooting_6">
         Troubleshooting
        </span>
       </h3>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Early automatic transmissions are a weak point in the E46.  The first symptom of a failing transmission is the inability to engage reverse gear.  This issue plagues early E46 owners including 323/328 owners. If you have a 323/328 and think you have the no-reverse problem, check out this thread. It has information on how you might be able to fix your no-reverse issue if you have a GM transmission:
         <a class="external free" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=706809" rel="nofollow">
          http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=706809
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Another GM "no reverse" thread can be found here:
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=458451" rel="nofollow">
          here
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         If you have an SMG/SSG transmission, there is a seal that often fails.  A machine shop in Malaysia has made a better replacement... check [this thread
         <a class="external free" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?p=3683902" rel="nofollow">
          http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?p=3683902
         </a>
         ] for details.
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Discussion and possible fix of p0720 error (output speed sensor circuit) can be found
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=560151" rel="nofollow">
          here
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
       <ul>
        <li>
         Resetting TM adaptations can sometimes help with fault codes.  You can reset the TM to the factory settings by doing the following:
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        1)Insert the Key into the ignition (DONT HOLD THE BRAKE).
2)Turn the key, just so the car electronics start and show the Engine light is on. (Dont START the Engine).
3)Press and HOLD the accelerater all the way down for 25 seconds.
4)After those 25 Seconds, proceed to Starting the Engine and drive your car.
       </p>
       <p>
        If done correctly you should feel the car to be more responsive and shift better as it resets the memory in the transmission.
       </p>
       <h2>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="HVAC_-_Ventilation_.26_A.2FC_.2F_Climate_Control">
         HVAC - Ventilation &amp; A/C / Climate Control
        </span>
       </h2>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="I_hear_a_beep_at_37_degrees_fahrenheit_.283_degrees_celsius.29._Why.3F">
         I hear a beep at 37 degrees fahrenheit (3 degrees celsius). Why?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        All BMWs will beep once the temperature reaches (or is below, if you're just starting your car) 37 degrees fahrenheit.  This is to warn of the possibility of black ice.  A dealer can disable the chime.  It's a bit of an annoing feature and always sends people thinking "What's wrong with my car now ...." This question comes up on the forum every winter:)
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Switching_between_Fahrenheit_and_Celsius">
         Switching between Fahrenheit and Celsius
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        To switch between F and C on the auto climate control, press the AUTO and FRONT DEFROST buttons at the same time, then release.
       </p>
       <h3>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Troubleshooting_7">
         Troubleshooting
        </span>
       </h3>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Erratic_fan_speed.3F">
         Erratic fan speed?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <ul>
        <li>
         The most common problem with the climate control system is a bad final stage resistor.  The symptoms of this are erratic fan speed (fan blowing at full speed while the display shows a low fan speed).   You can find replacement information
         <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=256286&amp;highlight=final+stage+resistor" rel="nofollow">
          here
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         FSU (aka blower motor resistor) replacement pictorial DIY by Starless is here:
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=472392" rel="nofollow">
          click here
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         If the fan speed DOES match the graph display, but it is constantly/incorrectly adjusting speed *OR* if the climate control unit won't turn off or on, you MAY need to replace the climate control module (IHKA). In the case of constantly/incorrectly adjusting fan speed, try replacing the final stage resistor first.
        </li>
        <li>
         If your climate control won't turn off OR on, the problem is likely the climate control module (IHKA).  If the problem is intermittent, you can usually 'reset' it by pulling out the appropriate fuses for a few seconds.
        </li>
        <li>
         To test electrically for a bad fan vs. bad fsu vs. bad module, see this
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=630061&amp;highlight=" rel="nofollow">
          post
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Does_your_driver.27s_side_A.2FC_blow_colder_than_the_passenger_side.3F">
         Does your driver's side A/C blow colder than the passenger side?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        As wrong as this sounds, that means the car is low on refrigerant (R134A).  BMWs have a "dual" A/C system that 'favors' the driver's side when the refrigerant runs low.  You should be able to pick up a R134A refill kit at a local auto parts store.
       </p>
       <p>
        See Wingspan's DIYs on how to refill the refrigerant
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showpost.php?p=2925892&amp;postcount=6" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        and
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showpost.php?p=4208498&amp;postcount=89" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <p>
        Thread with high/low side pressure chart
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=619636" rel="nofollow">
         here
        </a>
        , as well as a link to a/c troubleshooting.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="A.2FC_Evaporator.2FExpansion_Valve_DIY_.28you_won.27t_believe_the_pics.29">
         A/C Evaporator/Expansion Valve DIY (you won't believe the pics)
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        See
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=468090" rel="nofollow">
         this thread
        </a>
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Musty.28Gym_Sock.29_Smell_from_Vents.3F">
         Musty(Gym Sock) Smell from Vents?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        See
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?p=7354982#post7354982" rel="nofollow">
         this thread
        </a>
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Getting_constant_heat_even_when_the_AC_is_on.3F">
         Getting constant heat even when the AC is on?
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        Your heater valve could have failed open, constantly heating the air inside the car.  The valve opens to flow hot coolant through the heater core for heat in the car, but should close when heat is not needed.  Here's a good DIY for replacing this part:
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=617301&amp;highlight=heater+valve" rel="nofollow">
         Thread 1
        </a>
       </p>
       <p>
        If it's just warm air from some vents (and NOT the passenger side scenario described above indicating low refrigerant) it could be a problem with the control flaps inside the vent system.  Sometimes the vent flap motors (controlling the flaps in the vents that route air to footwells/dash/windshield etc.) will fail or the flaps break.  A fuse for the flap motors can blow too.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="I_hear_a_.22cricket.2Fscreeching.22_from_my_vents">
         I hear a "cricket/screeching" from my vents
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        The climate control fan either becomes unbalanced due to accumulation of dirt/dust, gets something caught in its housing (like a leaf or bug), or has worn out its bearings (or possibly just the electrical "brushes" that make it spin).  For DIY and other info., see this
        <a class="external text" href="http://forum.e46fanatics.com/showthread.php?t=418987" rel="nofollow">
         thread
        </a>
        .
       </p>
       <h2>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Parts.3F">
         Parts?
        </span>
       </h2>
       <p>
        RealOEM offers an online part number database for all BMWs.  Look up the part number for the part you need here:
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.realoem.com/bmw/" rel="nofollow">
         RealOEM
        </a>
        or
        <a class="external text" href="http://bmwfans.info/original/" rel="nofollow">
         BMW Fans
        </a>
        . With the part number in hand, you can now order OEM parts from your local BMW dealer or some of the below suppliers.
       </p>
       <p>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bavauto.com/" rel="nofollow">
         Bavarian Autosport
        </a>
        offers lots of OEM and great high end aftermarket parts.
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.pelicanparts.com/" rel="nofollow">
         Pelican Parts
        </a>
        is a good general supplier of reasonably priced OEM parts for your BMW and other imports.
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.autohausaz.com/" rel="nofollow">
         Arizona Autohaus
        </a>
        is also worthwhile checking.
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bramanautoparts.com/cat/BMW_2.aspx" rel="nofollow">
         Braman BMW Parts
        </a>
        is another option.
       </p>
       <p>
        There are a few BMW dealers that offer mail order parts at a discount:
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.mileoneparts.com/" rel="nofollow">
         Tischer BMW
        </a>
        is well known for its great service and
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.oembimmerparts.com/" rel="nofollow">
         OEM Bimmer Parts
        </a>
        (a bimmerfest sponsor).  Local dealers also may provide parts at a discount for BMWCCA members.
       </p>
       <p>
        Check out
        <a class="external text" href="http://frugalmechanic.com/" rel="nofollow">
         The Frugal Mechanic
        </a>
        to see who has the lowest price on replacement auto parts.
       </p>
       <h2>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="OTHER_See_also_.28M3.2C_Bentley_Service_Manual.2C_Other_Useful_Info.29">
         OTHER See also (M3, Bentley Service Manual, Other Useful Info)
        </span>
       </h2>
       <ul>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/index.php/BMW_E46_M3" title="BMW E46 M3">
          BMW E46 M3
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
       <p>
        The
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bentleypublishers.com/bmw/repair-information/bmw-3-series-e46-1999-2005-repair-manual.html" rel="nofollow">
         BMW 3 Series (E46) Service Manual
        </a>
        from
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bentleypublishers.com/" rel="nofollow">
         Bentley Publishers
        </a>
        is considered a reference work for repair procedures and a must-have for any DIY'er.
       </p>
       <h4>
        <span class="mw-headline" id="Locked_Key_in_Cabin_or_Trunk.2FDead_key_and_broken_door_lock_combo">
         Locked Key in Cabin or Trunk/Dead key and broken door lock combo
        </span>
       </h4>
       <p>
        See
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.bimmerfest.com/forums/showthread.php?t=452563" rel="nofollow">
         this thread
        </a>
        for opening your trunk without a key.  Going through the ski-pass in the middle is also a relatively clean way.  If your pass-thru isn't openable, you can drill a hole and try to work a coat hangar hook through there to grab the glow in the dark emergency release handle inside the trunk.
       </p>
       <p>
        If you have a dead keyfob in connection with a broken lock cylinder, the best method is to try to revive your dead keyfob with a temporary fresh battery (see electrical section of wiki for full battery replacement DIY).  A simple 3v calculator battery can be wired to your open keyfob in a pinch for a very temporary work around until you can replace the rechargeable battery.
       </p>
       <p>
        If you can't get in using a key, the top corner of the driver's door or passenger's door may be gently pried open a little and then propped open to allow a coat hangar (or simliar) to be slid in to grab one of the interior door handles for the double-pull.  Wrap the prying tools and coat hangar in protective tape so finishes do not get scratched.  Pushing the unlock button will not work as the computer has built in security routines to prevent such a "break-in" attempt.  If the car has been locked with a keyfob remote, the double-pulls will be disabled, but they can be re-enabled by pressing the central lock button by the parking brake handle.  Due to the design of the locking mechanism in the doors, a traditional "slim jim" approach will not work.
       </p>
       <p>
        Key cylinder repair DIY can be found in Exterior/Troubleshooting above
